{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1030}} The Tathāgata Buddha, knowing it was time, That hero adorned with all qualities, Who illuminates countless realms, The Bhagavān, the lion of men, set forth. {xxxi}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1031}} Avalokiteśvara, Mahā­sthāma­prāpta, {{note:{index:427,id:UT22084-055-001-1032}}} and Amoghadarśin; {{note:{index:428,id:UT22084-055-001-1033}}} Gandhahasti, Ratnakusuma, {{note:{index:429,id:UT22084-055-001-1034}}} and Ratnabāhu; {{note:{index:430,id:UT22084-055-001-1035}}} And Ratnaketu, Durabhisambhava, {{note:{index:431,id:UT22084-055-001-1036}}} Vīrasena, {{note:{index:432,id:UT22084-055-001-1037}}} And others followed in the Jina’s footsteps. {{note:{index:433,id:UT22084-055-001-1038}}} {xxxii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1039}} On his right was Ajita, who is named Maitraka, {{note:{index:434,id:UT22084-055-001-1040}}} Who has the wealth of infinite qualities, Who will become the following buddha And has completed the accumulation of merit and wisdom. {xxxiii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1041}} He is one who has cultivated {{note:{index:435,id:UT22084-055-001-1042}}} love, rejoicing, and equanimity. He is a great being of the Dharma who has developed compassion. He understands the infinite qualities, the qualities of the Lord of sages. {{note:{index:436,id:UT22084-055-001-1043}}} {xxxiv}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1044}} He followed behind {{note:{index:437,id:UT22084-055-001-1045}}} the compassionate Sugata And was followed by those {{note:{index:438,id:UT22084-055-001-1046}}} who will be Those with great realization in the Good Eon: The thousand buddhas less four, {xxxv}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1047}} Who were preceded by Maitraka. And also he who in the past, in this city of Rājagṛha, While born in divine bodies that were like beautiful moonlight, Made infinite offerings to jinas throughout eons, {xxxvi}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1048}} That hero Candraprabha was also present at the front. To the left of the one with supreme compassion Was Mañjuśrī, {{note:{index:439,id:UT22084-055-001-1049}}} along with many thousands of millions {{note:{index:440,id:UT22084-055-001-1050}}} Of heroes who have sublime qualities of miraculous powers, {{note:{index:441,id:UT22084-055-001-1051}}} {xxxvii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1052}} Who traveled to endless hundreds of realms. Following him were those in the śrāvaka saṅgha: Śārisuta, {{note:{index:442,id:UT22084-055-001-1053}}} Maudgalyāyana, {{note:{index:443,id:UT22084-055-001-1054}}} Kāla, Kāśyapa, Subhūti, Nanda, and Kapphiṇa; {xxxviii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1055}} Bhadrikarāja, {{note:{index:444,id:UT22084-055-001-1056}}} and similarly Kauṇḍinya; Ānanda, and similarly Sthavira Rāhula; And Svāgata, Kañcika, {{note:{index:445,id:UT22084-055-001-1057}}} Pūrṇa, Udāyin, Revata, Kauṣṭhila, {{note:{index:446,id:UT22084-055-001-1058}}} Upāli, and Aniruddha. {xxxix}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1059}} A full nine thousand {{note:{index:447,id:UT22084-055-001-1060}}} of those with matted hair {{page:{number:67,folio:F.34.b}}} Followed behind the śrāvaka saṅgha. They were all mighty ascetics who knew the Vedas and the rituals, {{note:{index:448,id:UT22084-055-001-1061}}} And had mastered curses, renunciation, and beneficial incantations. {{note:{index:449,id:UT22084-055-001-1062}}} {xl}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1063}} Self-controlled rishis with peaceful minds, With disciplined minds, bowing with palms together, Followed behind the Buddha, the lamp of the world, The lion of men, endowed with compassion, {xli}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1064}} The liberator of thousands of beings, as he proceeded. Like the completely pure lord of the host of stars, The full moon of the last month of autumn, {{note:{index:450,id:UT22084-055-001-1065}}} The Teacher who is without equal was encircled {xlii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1066}} By many hundred thousands of Brahmās. As he stepped on the threshold of the city’s gateway, The earth and its thick forests shook. The devas, asuras, {{note:{index:451,id:UT22084-055-001-1067}}} and mahoragas {xliii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1068}} Scattered excellent flowers and supreme incense. {{note:{index:452,id:UT22084-055-001-1069}}} {xliv}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1070}} The moment the Bhagavān placed his right foot, adorned by a precious wheel from the accumulation of countless roots of merit, upon the threshold of the gate, this universe of a thousand million worlds shook in six ways. It trembled, trembled strongly, and trembled intensely; it quivered, quivered strongly, and quivered intensely; it shook, shook strongly, and shook intensely; it shuddered, shuddered strongly, and shuddered intensely; it quaked, quaked strongly, and quaked intensely; the east sank and the west rose, the west sank and the east rose, the north sank and the south rose, the south sank and the north rose, the perimeter sank and the center rose, and the center sank and the perimeter rose. A great radiance shone in the world, and countless, numberless other amazing, wonderful, miraculous manifestations appeared. {{note:{index:453,id:UT22084-055-001-1071}}}
The nature of this is described in these verses:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1073}} When the Guide came to that supreme city And placed his supreme foot upon the gateway’s threshold, That magnificence caused this earth to shake, And the beings in this supreme city were overjoyed. {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1074}} When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold The people who were hungry and thirsty {{page:{number:68,folio:F.35.a}}} At that time became free of the need to eat or drink. They became free of hunger and thirst. {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1075}} When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold All those people who were blind, Deaf, and had no protector and little merit Were all able to see and hear. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1076}} When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold All the pretas in the realm of Yama, Suffering greatly and eating snot and spit, Were touched by light and became happy. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1077}} When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold The supreme trees—the sal and the karnikara— At the summit of crags and on mountaintops, They all bowed toward the Buddha. {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1078}} When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold The entire ground shook in six ways Throughout the villages and towns as far as the ocean, Without causing harm to anyone. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1079}} Devas, humans, kumbhāṇḍas, and rākṣasas— Wherever beings lived, there was happiness and joy. They developed faith in supreme, sublime enlightenment And held a parasol for the guide of the world. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1080}} When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold, Thousands of musical instruments sounded without being played; Hearing the beautiful sound of music, All beings were filled with joy. {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1081}} Hundreds of thousands of trees bowed down, And all flowers blossomed at that time. Hundreds of thousands of devas in the sky Made nonhuman offerings to the Jina. {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1082}} When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold, Hundreds {{note:{index:454,id:UT22084-055-001-1083}}} of bulls {{note:{index:455,id:UT22084-055-001-1084}}} lowed with joy. The kings of horses and elephants {{note:{index:456,id:UT22084-055-001-1085}}} raised their bodies; The lions, the kings of animals, roared. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1086}} The kings, the rulers, however many there were, Came from the cardinal and intermediate directions. When they saw the glorious majesty of the Jina, With minds filled with joy they bowed to him. {11}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1087}} Some praised the Lord of the World; Some scattered a rain of flowers on the Jina; Some placed their ten fingers together in homage, And they cried, “Oh, the Jina, compassionate one!” {12}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1088}} Some scattered excellent strings of pearls {{page:{number:69,folio:F.35.b}}} And various ornaments that give rise to joy, And some scattered clothing and jewels. They developed the supreme, unequaled aspiration to enlightenment. {13}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1089}} Some scattered excellent meshes of gold; Some also scattered mukhaphullaka adornments. Some scattered excellent ornaments of gold, And some, likewise, scattered anklets. {{note:{index:457,id:UT22084-055-001-1090}}} {14}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1091}} Some scattered excellent bracelets, {{note:{index:458,id:UT22084-055-001-1092}}} Some scattered armlets inset with jewels, And some aspired to enlightenment, scattering excellent Pieces of cloth, {{note:{index:459,id:UT22084-055-001-1093}}} saying, “May we become buddhas!” {15}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1094}} When the Lord of the World stood in the gateway, Some people scattered golden necklaces. Some with minds filled with faith scattered excellent crest jewels; {{note:{index:460,id:UT22084-055-001-1095}}} Some scattered networks of jewels. {16}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1096}} Those beings who were in extreme suffering, Tormented by many kinds of miseries, All attained happiness through the majesty Of the Guide, the supreme human. {17}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1097}} Cuckoos, mynas, and peacocks, And similarly cranes and other water birds {{note:{index:461,id:UT22084-055-001-1098}}} — All the flocks of birds were in the sky Emitting their beautiful, perfect songs. {18}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1099}} Desire, anger, and ignorance Ceased in whoever heard The sweet, beautiful songs Of those flocks of joyous birds. {19}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1100}} The millions of beings who heard that joyful sound All attained the patience that is concordant with the Dharma. The Sugata gave them all this prophecy: “You will in the future become buddhas.” {20}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1101}} At that time the kleśas did not arise, And everyone was respectful to the Dharma king. {{note:{index:462,id:UT22084-055-001-1102}}} {21}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1103}} At that time, when they saw the form of the Guide’s body, {{note:{index:463,id:UT22084-055-001-1104}}} They developed the aspiration for the supreme wisdom of buddhahood. They wondered, “When will we attain this kind of wisdom?” And the Jina, knowing that, gave them their prophecies. {22}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1105}} From each pore of the Sugata There shone hundreds of thousands of light rays And more, as many as there are sand grains in the Ganges— It would not be possible to perceive all their attributes. {23}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1106}} At that time, the sunlight did not shine. Nor was there light from jewels, fire, or the devas. {{page:{number:70,folio:F.36.a}}} There was no other light at that time When there was the splendor of the Buddha entering the city. {24}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1107}} When with that great assembly the Sugata proceeded on the path, Wherever the feet of the one with the ten strengths trod There appeared from the ground a hundred thousand lotuses That were pure and had ten thousand million petals. {25}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1108}} When the Guide entered the supreme city, At that time there was no dirt or refuse. Throughout the entire city there arose The lovely aroma of the most fragrant incense. {26}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1109}} The entire city and its streets were purified. They had no stones or gravel and were sprinkled with perfume And bestrewn with the petals of various kinds of flowers. That is the kind of merit the one with ten strengths had. {27}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1110}} When a hundred thousand yakṣas with ferocious minds Saw the Buddha, the Lord of men who was like gold, They felt an immense love for the Guide And took refuge in the Buddha, Dharma, and Saṅgha. {28}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1111}} All of the million millions {{note:{index:464,id:UT22084-055-001-1112}}} of devas Who had come to see the Lord of men {{note:{index:465,id:UT22084-055-001-1113}}} Let fall a rain of flowers on the Sugata. They scattered flowers while in the middle of the sky. {29}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1114}} The flowers scattered by humans for the Jina Formed a parasol of flowers in the sky. The flowers scattered by the devas Were strewn on the ground as divine flowers. {30}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1115}} The devas, humans, kumbhāṇḍas, and rākṣasas Never tired of gazing upon him. When they saw the Lord {{note:{index:466,id:UT22084-055-001-1116}}} with the ten strengths, They were overjoyed and felt the highest delight. {31}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1117}} When they saw the body of the supreme being, All beings were overjoyed and delighted; They did not even think of the divine flowers, Which did not seem at all wonderful. {{note:{index:467,id:UT22084-055-001-1118}}} {32}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1119}} Brahmā upon the right of the one with ten strengths, Śakra, the king of the devas, on his left, And the many millions of deities in the middle of the sky Showed great veneration to the supreme being. {33}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1120}} Devas and asuras encircled the Jina, Who eclipsed all the majesty of devas and humans. With the soles of his feet making patterns on the ground, The invited Bhagavān entered into the city. {34}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1121}} His body was beautified by excellent primary signs, Like the firmament filled with stars. {{page:{number:71,folio:F.36.b}}} The Buddha shone upon the king’s road {{note:{index:468,id:UT22084-055-001-1122}}} Like the full moon in the sky. {35}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1123}} Just as an excellent, pure, precious jewel That is free of all impurities shines So that a pure light goes in all directions, {{note:{index:469,id:UT22084-055-001-1124}}} In that way the Jina illuminated the entire world. {36}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1125}} Devas and asuras encircled the Jina. The supreme human who entered Rājagṛha With the soles of his feet leaving patterns on the ground, The Buddha, came to the home of the youth Candraprabha. {37}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1126}} The supreme city was perfectly adorned, Millions of banners had been erected, The entire ground was anointed with the best perfumes, And beautiful summer flowers were scattered. {38}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1127}} When the Sugata spoke to teach With compassion for the people in the streets, The Jina manifested emanations That taught to them the excellent Dharma of the Buddha. {39}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1128}} [The Jina manifested emanations; Bodies that were like gold were manifested. The Buddha, the Jina, through his emanations, Remained in emptiness, peace, the enlightenment of buddhahood.] {{note:{index:470,id:UT22084-055-001-1129}}} {40}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1130}} When the hundreds of thousands of beings heard that, They prayed for the supreme wisdom of the Buddha, Wondering, “When will I attain this kind of wisdom?” Knowing their thoughts, the Jina prophesied to them. {{note:{index:471,id:UT22084-055-001-1131}}} {41}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1132}} There were those who aspired to attain That inconceivable supreme attainment. They had invited the Jina, the Lord of men, And there was no limit to the offerings they made. {{note:{index:472,id:UT22084-055-001-1133}}} {42}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1134}} There were those who developed an excellent aspiration, Thinking, “I will tomorrow invite the compassionate one, He who wishes to benefit beings, Whom it is difficult to see in saṃsāra.” {{note:{index:473,id:UT22084-055-001-1135}}} {43}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1136}} Some who were upon the roofs Developed the sublime, supreme aspiration to enlightenment And they scattered divine flowers on the handsome, Beautifully adorned body of the one with the ten strengths. {44}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1137}} Some developed the supreme, highest aspiration And scattered garlands of magnolias, Kachnar flowers, the scents of summer, And wreaths of silken ribbons. {45}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1138}} Some stood, holding excellent flowers, Their bodies perfectly beautified by their raiment. They held various flowers and wreaths of silk That they cast in the direction of the Jina with great power. {{note:{index:474,id:UT22084-055-001-1139}}} {46}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1140}} Some scattered red lotuses, night lotuses, Blue lotuses, and excellent golden flowers. {{page:{number:72,folio:F.37.a}}} Some scattered precious flowers, {{note:{index:475,id:UT22084-055-001-1141}}} And some scattered sandalwood powder. {47}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1142}} When the Guide entered the supreme city The wonders that appeared were uncountable, Unequaled, impossible to describe, And they brought many millions of beings to buddha wisdom. {48}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1143}} Those in Avṛha, Atapa, who had seen the truth, The devas of Sudṛśa and Sudarśana, And those in Akaniṣṭha, who are free of desire— They all came to see the Lord of humans. {49}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1144}} Similarly, countless Parī­ttaśubha {{note:{index:476,id:UT22084-055-001-1145}}} devas, Apramāṇaśubha {{note:{index:477,id:UT22084-055-001-1146}}} devas, filled with joy, And countless millions of Śubhakṛtsna devas Came to see the Guide, the great Rishi. {50}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1147}} Countless Apramāṇābha devas, And similarly the Parī­ttābha devas, And countless millions of Ābhāsvara devas Came to see the Lord of the World. {{note:{index:478,id:UT22084-055-001-1148}}} {51}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1149}} Many hundreds of thousands of Brahmā’s entourage, {{note:{index:479,id:UT22084-055-001-1150}}} And similarly the faithful Brahmapurohita devas And many hundreds of Brahmakāyika devas, All came so as to see the Guide. {52}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1151}} Also the Para­nirmita­vaśa­vartin {{note:{index:480,id:UT22084-055-001-1152}}} devas, And the pure beings who dwell in Nirmāṇaratin, And the joyful devas of Tuṣita and Yāma All came to pay homage to the Buddha. {53}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1153}} Śakra, king of the devas, and the Trāyastriṃśa {{note:{index:481,id:UT22084-055-001-1154}}} devas {{note:{index:482,id:UT22084-055-001-1155}}} Came with hundreds of millions of apsarases And they sent down a rain of flowers, Having come to see the Buddha, the Lord of sages. {54}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1156}} Also the world guardians of the four directions Vaiśravaṇa, Dhṛtarāṣṭra the nāga king, {{note:{index:483,id:UT22084-055-001-1157}}} Virūḍhaka, and Virūpākṣa, their minds filled with joy, All came in order to praise the Lord of men. {55}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1158}} Ailavila, the powerful king of the yakṣas, With a delighted mind and encircled by a hundred yakṣas, Was in the middle of the sky and joyfully They sent down a rain of numerous various flowers. {56}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1159}} Also the Sadāmatta {{note:{index:484,id:UT22084-055-001-1160}}} and Mālādhāra devas, Holding various kinds of incense and flowers, With their retinues, all joyful, {{page:{number:73,folio:F.37.b}}} Made offerings there to the supreme individual. {57}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1161}} Also numerous Karoṭapāṇi yakṣas And adorned yakṣa maidens Made offerings to the Buddha With hundreds of compositions of The beautiful, melodious music of the yakṣas. {58}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1162}} Druma, the king of the kiṃnaras, With thousands of kiṃnara maidens skilled In sweet and melodious songs and music, Arrived from Gandhamādana to make offerings to the supreme Jina. {59}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1163}} Śambara, Bala, Vemacitra, and Rāhu, Together with an entourage of thousands of asura maidens, And together with crowds of other powerful asuras, Came and sent down a rain of jewels. {60}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1164}} From countless trillions of rākṣasas A thousand million rākṣasas honored him. They respectfully scattered a multitude of various Flower petals upon the supreme individual. {{note:{index:485,id:UT22084-055-001-1165}}} {61}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1166}} The nāga king Girivalgu, With a great entourage came before the Tathāgata, Holding great numbers of perfect, precious flowers, And bowed down at the Sugata’s feet. {{note:{index:486,id:UT22084-055-001-1167}}} {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1168}} The nāga lords Padma and Mahāpadma, And also Vāsuki, Ananta, and Phanaka, {{note:{index:487,id:UT22084-055-001-1169}}} Came before the great leader And respectfully bowed to the Sugata. {ii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1170}} The nāga king Maṇi, filled with joy, Came before the feet of the great leader Holding fragrant, perfect nāga flowers And sat before the Sugata at no great distance. {iii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1171}} Also the nāga king Anavatapta, With perfectly trained nāga maidens Playing a hundred thousand musical instruments and drums, Came and made offerings there to the Lord of the World. {62}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1172}} The five hundred sons of Anavatapta, Encircled by their kindred and filled with joy, Seeking the highest, vast wisdom, Came to make offerings to the self-arisen one. {63}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1173}} Similarly, the nāga king Apalāla, Palms together, bowed to the supreme individual Holding beautiful, excellent nāga pearls. He remained in the sky, making offerings to the king of sages. {64}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1174}} Similarly, the nāga king Mucilinda, With great happiness and filled with joy, Holding various jewels and pearls, {{page:{number:74,folio:F.38.a}}} Came and scattered them for the Guide. {65}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1175}} Similarly, the nāga king Kālika Came before the Tathāgata. Joyful and holding perfect, beautiful strings of jewels, He made offerings to the supreme individual. {{note:{index:488,id:UT22084-055-001-1176}}} {66}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1177}} He {{note:{index:489,id:UT22084-055-001-1178}}} felt great veneration as he thought Of the qualities of the Tathāgata. Encircled by his many nāga kindred, He recited many praises of the Guide. {67}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1179}} Similarly, the nāga kings Nanda and Upananda— Similarly, also, Takṣaka and Kṛṣṇagautama— Came there gazing upon the Jina And bowed down to the Sugata’s feet. {68}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1180}} The nāga king Elapatra Came weeping, encircled by a hundred nāgas. He remembered the supreme sage Jina Kāśyapa And saw what an unfavorable rebirth he himself had obtained. {69}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1181}} “Alas! I had doubts in the past. In the past I cut down an elapatra {{note:{index:490,id:UT22084-055-001-1182}}} bush, {{note:{index:491,id:UT22084-055-001-1183}}} And therefore I obtained this unfavorable rebirth. It is not easy to know the Dharma of the Jina. {70}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1184}} “I forsake this rebirth into a nāgī’s womb, And this birth in an extremely detestable body. I will realize the Dharma, the state of peace, That the best of men realized in the Bodhimaṇḍa.” {71}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1185}} Sāgara, the nāga cakravartin king, Accompanied by an entourage of thirty million nāgas, And the majestic Varuṇa, holding necklaces of jewels, Came in order to make offerings to the Bhagavān. {{note:{index:492,id:UT22084-055-001-1186}}} {72}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1187}} The yakṣa of Rājagṛha who caught While he was in the sky The rock thrown at the Buddha Was respectfully present before the Sugata. {73}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1188}} The entire domain of the king of Alakavatī {{note:{index:493,id:UT22084-055-001-1189}}} Became empty, with no yakṣa remaining there. They had all promised each other To come and see the Lord of the World. {74}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1190}} In the same way, Kharakarṇa and Sūciromā, The terrifying yakṣas of the forests, And the yakṣa Gardabhaka, who lives in the snow mountains, Had come into the presence of the self-arisen Jina. {{note:{index:494,id:UT22084-055-001-1191}}} {75}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1192}} Indraketu, Vikaṭa, and Surūpa, Bakula, Pañcika, and Śākyavardhana, {{note:{index:495,id:UT22084-055-001-1193}}} And a thousand other yakṣa lords {{page:{number:75,folio:F.38.b}}} Came holding censers of incense. {{note:{index:496,id:UT22084-055-001-1194}}} {76}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1195}} Many with ugly, misshapen bodies, Many kinds of bodies, destitute of adornment, In their hundreds of thousands Came into his presence, holding yakṣa flowers. {77}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1196}} Gautama, Rishi Bṛhaspati, and Jahnu, Kauśika, Kāśyapa, and Markandeya, Viśvāmitra, Parāśara, and Gargā, They all came to pay homage to the Buddha. {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1197}} And similarly, there were the joyous and enraptured Nārada, And the rishis Vyāsa, Kutsa, and Aṅgiras, And Manu, Bhṛgu, Vātsyāyana, and Vaśiṣṭha, Who came to pay homage to the Buddha. {ii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1198}} Jaimini, Vāmana, {{note:{index:497,id:UT22084-055-001-1199}}} and Vaiśampāyana, Jamadagni and supreme rishi Vālmīki, Durvāsa, and also Cyavana Came to the supreme city to see the Guide. {iii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1200}} When they saw the Rishi, the rishis were overjoyed And they bowed down to the feet of the king of sages. They paid homage to the lamp of the world and praised him, Standing before the Hero with palms placed together. {iv}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1201}} The entire multitude of rishis in the world Came in order to see the Lord of men. When they saw him they made vast offerings And stood before him with palms placed together. {v}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1202}} The garuḍas that live at the ocean’s shore Came, having transformed into the appearance of brahmins. Holding various beautiful kinds of crowns And positioned in the sky, they paid homage to the Sugata. {78}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1203}} All of the devas that dwell in Jambudvīpa, Whether in hundreds of towns or in its forests, And all the goddesses of the towns Came and made offerings to the Lord. {79}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1204}} The countless devas of the forests And all the mountain devas came, And also the countless devas of rivers {{note:{index:498,id:UT22084-055-001-1205}}} Arrived to make offerings to the Guide. {80}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1206}} The hundreds of devas of desert wildernesses, All the devas of mountain peaks, The devas of lakes, springs, and ponds, And the devas of the ocean came into the Buddha’s presence. {81}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1207}} Assemblies of devas, asuras, and nāgas, Yakṣas, kiṃnaras, mahoragas, and garuḍas, {{page:{number:76,folio:F.39.a}}} And similarly, a multitude of pretas and pūtanas Showed their respect to the supreme being. {82}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1208}} They made offerings to the supreme Jina When the Guide entered the supreme city. The kings of the devas, asuras, nāgas, and yakṣas Could not get their fill of looking at him. {83}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1209}} In previous existences the Lord of the World Had made perfect offerings to the jinas of the past. This was the ripened result of that merit. The beings could not stop looking at the Lord of humans. {84}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1210}} When the Jina shone light through the buddha realm, Meru, and similarly Sumeru and Cakravāla The Himagiri and Gandhamādana Could not obscure the Jina’s light. {85}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1211}} All of the oceans in this buddha realm At that time all became land, And the entirety of this buddha realm Became equally scattered with flowers. {86}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1212}} Countless hundreds of thousands of light rays Came from the soles of the King of Dharma’s feet. All the beings in the hells were cooled And, freed from suffering, experienced happiness. {87}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1213}} The one with the ten strengths taught the Dharma So that the sight of devas and humans was purified. Countless hundreds of thousands of beings All gained certainty in the Buddha’s wisdom. {88}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1214}} The numerous miracles manifested by the Sugata Could not easily be described in ten million eons. When the Guide entered the supreme city All beings rejoiced at the Jina, the Sugata. {{note:{index:499,id:UT22084-055-001-1215}}} {89}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1216}} These qualities of the Sugata are immeasurable. They are the supreme human’s perfection of qualities. They have transcended all unique qualities. Bow your heads to the realm of the Buddha’s merit! {90}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1217}} Conclusion of the tenth chapter, “The Entry into the City.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1218}} The Bhagavān came to the street on which was the home of the youth Candraprabha, and soon arrived at the home of the youth Candraprabha. Once he had arrived, he sat on the seat prepared for him. The saṅgha of bodhisattvas and the saṅgha of bhikṣus also sat on the appropriate seats that had been arranged for each of them.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1219}} Then the youth Candraprabha, knowing that the Bhagavān, the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, and the saṅgha of bhikṣus were seated, {{page:{number:77,folio:F.39.b}}} himself presented and served a series of great offerings: numerous excellent foods, with hundreds of flavors to savor as they chewed, licked, sucked, and drank.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1220}} When he saw that the Bhagavān had concluded his meal, which was signaled by his setting down his alms bowl, {{note:{index:500,id:UT22084-055-001-1221}}} he offered for the Bhagavān’s body two lengths of cloth {{note:{index:501,id:UT22084-055-001-1222}}} of the value of a trillion silver coins, {{note:{index:502,id:UT22084-055-001-1223}}} and also to each of the bodhisattvas, and he offered three dharma robes to each one in the saṅgha of bhikṣus.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1224}} Then the youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder and, casting toward the Bhagavān a divine coral tree flower, he made offerings and uttered praises. Then, his palms placed together, he bowed toward the Bhagavān and praised him with these appropriate verses: {{note:{index:503,id:UT22084-055-001-1225}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1226}} “You are unborn and unceasing; Without a body, inconceivable, You have the perfect body and primary signs. I pay homage to you who are an ocean of qualities. {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1227}} “You are a hero who has been born from wisdom. You possess the power of methods and strengths. You are a buddha who is the same as space. I pay homage to you who have perfected patience. {ii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1228}} “Your conduct is to remain in constant mindfulness. The Tathāgata’s bed is joy and happiness. Your drink is samādhi and your food is supreme dhyāna. I pay homage to you who reside in the solitude of emptiness. {iii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1229}} “O Inconceivable Buddha, The Guide for the whole world! When the beings of this world make offerings to you They advance toward supreme nirvāṇa.” {iv}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1230}} Thus did he praise the one unequaled Lord, and then the youth said, with a joyous mind, “Unequaled Buddha, who has an inconceivable body, you have consumed the meal. Through this may I also become a buddha like you, the god of gods!” {{page:{number:78,folio:F.40.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1231}} In that way, therefore, the youth Candraprabha provided divine food with a hundred flavors to the Bhagavān. He offered divine coral tree flowers to the Bhagavān, and praised him with appropriate verses.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1232}} Now, placing his palms together in homage toward the Bhagavān, in his mind he addressed him with these verses:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1233}} “Whatever the wise bodhisattvas do, They always follow the nature of the Dharma. I pray to the Guide to teach what actions are performed When those with wisdom engage in actions. {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1234}} “In what way, Guide, are past lives remembered? In what way is rebirth in a womb avoided? In what way does the community not become divided? In what way does one gain endless eloquence? {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1235}} “You know the activities of all beings. You have the knowledge of all phenomena. You are the invincible, supreme human. I have asked my questions; give me your elucidation. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1236}} “You know that nonexistence is the nature of phenomena; You put into words that which cannot be described. Just as a lion overpowers all jackals, {{note:{index:504,id:UT22084-055-001-1237}}} That is how the Buddha overpowers the tīrthikas. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1238}} “You know the conduct of all beings. You have the wisdom of all phenomena. You have wisdom without attachment, and activity that is pure. Lord of the Dharma, elucidate those for me. {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1239}} “You know the past and also the future. You also know what is happening in the present. You have unimpeded knowledge of the three times. Therefore I have asked you my questions, lion of the Śākyas. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1240}} “You, Dharma king, know the true nature That is the nature of the jinas of the three times. You are skilled in the nature of phenomena, self-arisen one. Therefore, ocean of wisdom, I have asked you my questions. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1241}} “You do not have any quality of error. Therefore you have a mind of complete elimination— You have eliminated the fetters and the rigidity of ignorance. Lord of humans, teach me the conduct of a bodhisattva. {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1242}} “You, Jina, know the characteristics of phenomena. Teach me the characteristics of phenomena. {{page:{number:79,folio:F.40.b}}} When I have understood those characteristics of phenomena I shall practice the conduct of enlightenment that has those characteristics. {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1243}} “The conduct of beings is infinitely different. How do they engage in practicing their conduct? Teach to me how conduct is engaged in So that from your words, I may know the conduct of beings. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1244}} “Different characteristics are characteristic of the nature of phenomena. Their essence {{note:{index:505,id:UT22084-055-001-1245}}} is empty and their nature {{note:{index:506,id:UT22084-055-001-1246}}} is pure. I pray that you teach me the way of phenomena That a bodhisattva directly perceives. {11}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1247}} “In this there is the perfect knowledge of all phenomena. There is skill in all the words of the teaching. There is no doubt; all doubt and uncertainty have been cut through. Teach me the enlightenment of buddhahood.” {12}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1248}} The Bhagavān, knowing the thoughts that were in the mind of the youth Candraprabha, said to him, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas will attain all these qualities, and they will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, if they possess just one quality. What is that one quality? Young man, it is when the bodhisattva mahāsattvas know the nature of all phenomena.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1249}} “Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas know the nature of all phenomena? Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas know that all phenomena are nameless; they have no names. They know that all phenomena have no vocalization, they have no expression in speech, they have no letters, they have no birth, they have no cessation, they have no characteristics of cause, they have no characteristics of conditions, {{note:{index:507,id:UT22084-055-001-1250}}} they are devoid of characteristics, they have the one characteristic of having no characteristics, they are devoid of attributes, they cannot be conceived of, they have no thought, and they have no mentality.”
Then the Bhagavān taught this in the following verses:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1252}} “The single teaching on phenomena Is that phenomena have no characteristics. That is the teaching of supreme wisdom From having true, correct knowledge. {13} {{page:{number:80,folio:F.41.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1253}} “The bodhisattvas who know That teaching on phenomena Will not cease from elucidation {{note:{index:508,id:UT22084-055-001-1254}}} Even though they teach ten million sūtras. {14}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1255}} “Through the blessing of the Guide The ultimate truth is known. When the ultimate is known There is nothing to be taught. {15}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1256}} “Through one thing, everything is known. Through one thing, everything is seen. However much they teach They will not become proud. {16}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1257}} “With their minds they have ascertained The selflessness of all phenomena, And as they are trained in teaching using terms, They speak with words that are correct. {17}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1258}} “Whatever sound they hear, They know its past. {{note:{index:509,id:UT22084-055-001-1259}}} Knowing the past {{note:{index:510,id:UT22084-055-001-1260}}} of that sound They are not captivated {{note:{index:511,id:UT22084-055-001-1261}}} by that sound. {18}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1262}} “Just like the past {{note:{index:512,id:UT22084-055-001-1263}}} of a sound, So are the characteristics of phenomena. Knowing phenomena to be like that They will not be reborn in a womb. {19}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1264}} “They know that all phenomena are unborn And that they have no origin. Knowing this teaching on birth {{note:{index:513,id:UT22084-055-001-1265}}} They always remember their previous lives. {20}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1266}} “When they remember those lives They perform their actions. For those who perform those actions Their community of followers remains united. {21}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1267}} “The bodhisattvas who know The emptiness of phenomena Will never be without that knowledge. It is the summit of nothingness. {22}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1268}} “When the foolish think about The summit of nothingness They continue in saṃsāra For millions of eons. {23}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1269}} “If they are able to understand it Just as the Guide knows it, Then they will have no suffering And they will not go to the lower realms. {24}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1270}} “All ordinary individuals Are ignorant of this nature. They reject this kind of Dharma That brings the cessation of suffering. {{note:{index:514,id:UT22084-055-001-1271}}} {25}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1272}} “Phenomena are perceived when No phenomena can be found. Recognize that perception When that perception occurs. {26}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1273}} “The foolish conceptualize Through consciousness and perception. The wise do not become ignorant In conceiving of phenomena. {27} {{page:{number:81,folio:F.41.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1274}} “The unpolluted phenomena of emptiness Are within the field of experience of the bodhisattvas. {{note:{index:515,id:UT22084-055-001-1275}}} This level of those who are wise Is not within the field of experience of the foolish. {28}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1276}} “This level of the bodhisattvas Is that of bodhisattva practice. It is the adornment of the Buddha’s Dharma. It is the peace and emptiness that has been taught. {29}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1277}} “When the bodhisattvas Eliminate their propensities They remain in the family of the buddhas And are not captured by form. {30}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1278}} “All phenomena are without location; They have no location that can be known. For the one who knows this about their location, Enlightenment is not difficult to attain. {31}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1279}} “Generosity, conduct, learning, and patience, And relying upon a good friend: {{note:{index:516,id:UT22084-055-001-1280}}} Those who know these activities Will quickly attain enlightenment. {32}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1281}} “Devas, nāgas, yakṣas, and asuras, Mahoragas and gandharvas, will always honor them. All the kings of the garuḍas, kiṃnaras, And rākṣasas {{note:{index:517,id:UT22084-055-001-1282}}} will make offerings to them. {33}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1283}} “Millions of buddhas will recite their praises Continuously for many millions of eons. It is not possible to reach the end Of such praise for one who teaches this Dharma. {34}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1284}} “The bodhisattvas who know emptiness Benefit many millions of beings. They kindly teach the Dharma to assemblies {{note:{index:518,id:UT22084-055-001-1285}}} And those who hear it are delighted and respectful.{35}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1286}} “They gain vast knowledge So that they see the supreme humans. They see the beautiful display of their realms And the lords of the worlds teach them the Dharma. {{note:{index:519,id:UT22084-055-001-1287}}} {36}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1288}} “Know that all phenomena are like illusions; Know that just as space is naturally empty, Phenomena are also naturally like that. In that way there will be no attachment in any kind of activity. {37}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1289}} “With unimpeded wisdom, benefiting others, Performing supreme bodhisattva conduct in the world, With wisdom examining all phenomena, They send emanations to other realms. {38}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1290}} “Those emanations accomplish buddha activities. They go naturally, just as is their nature. The beings who remain in the aspiration to enlightenment {{page:{number:82,folio:F.42.a}}} Will attain whatever goals they wish for. {39}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1291}} “Those who are steadfastly within the buddha family Will always honor the buddhas. Their bodies will shine brightly, Adorned by the thirty-two excellent signs. {40}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1292}} “They will attain the conduct that is within the supreme samādhi And an endless multitude of other benefits. They will always have great, unshakable strength And a majesty that outshines that of kings. {41}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1293}} “The wise who practice the Buddha’s Dharma Will have an excellent appearance and great beauty. Their merit and majesty and splendor will increase. Their majesty will outshine even that of the devas. {42}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1294}} “Those who steadfastly remain in the aspiration to enlightenment Will always be friends to all beings. There will never be any darkness In their teaching of the enlightenment of buddhahood. {43}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1295}} “The nature of phenomena is like that of space, Inexpressible, beyond speech and words. Those who know that supreme nature Will have an unceasing confidence in teaching. {44}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1296}} “Even though they teach a hundred thousand sūtras, They know the finest details of the past. The wise will always have unimpeded speech, Knowing the subtlety of the nature of phenomena. {45}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1297}} “They will be skilled {{note:{index:520,id:UT22084-055-001-1298}}} in hundreds of ways. They will have mastered the many kinds of words and definitions. They have certainty in the ripening {{note:{index:521,id:UT22084-055-001-1299}}} of actions and results. They become distinctively preeminent in that way. {46}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1300}} “They will possess unimpaired power. They are great wise ones, the heirs of those with the ten strengths. Knowing the subtle nature of phenomena, They will always have a completely pure memory. {{note:{index:522,id:UT22084-055-001-1301}}} {47}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1302}} “Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena, They will never hear an unpleasant sound. They always hear pleasant and melodious sounds And their words are always pleasant. {48}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1303}} “Because they know the very subtle nature of phenomena, They have memory, understanding, wisdom, and realization. Similarly, their minds are clear and unpolluted And they teach many hundreds of sūtras. {49}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1304}} “They are learned in the categories of letters and words. They know many different kinds of sounds, And they are skilled in meanings and letters. {{page:{number:83,folio:F.42.b}}} They have these qualities through knowing the nature of phenomena. {50}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1305}} “Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena They are always attractive and charming To devas, humans, nāgas, {{note:{index:523,id:UT22084-055-001-1306}}} and rākṣasas, Asuras, mahoragas, and kiṃnaras. {51}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1307}} “Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena They never perceive as frightening The extremely terrible and flesh-devouring Crowds of spirits, pretas, and rākṣasas. {52}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1308}} “Those who hear the vast {{note:{index:524,id:UT22084-055-001-1309}}} teaching of the wise Experience vast joy and their hairs stand on end. They develop a vast attraction to the buddhas, And gain a vast, inconceivable benefit. {{note:{index:525,id:UT22084-055-001-1310}}} {53}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1311}} “Even by speaking for many thousands of eons It is not possible to describe the power of the merit That comes from memorizing this Dharma treasure of the sugatas. It is immeasurable, infinite, and unquantifiable. {54}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1312}} “The jinas to whom offerings have been made in the past, The countless buddhas of the future, And the buddhas who are present in the ten directions, Are so by having memorized this supreme samādhi of peace. {55}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1313}} “If a person who wishes for merit, With immeasurable affection for them Serves compassionate ones with the ten strengths For countless endless millions of eons, {56}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1314}} “And if a second person who wishes for merit Memorizes, during future times, One verse from this way of the ultimate truth, Then the previous person’s merit will not even be a fraction of that. {57}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1315}} “This will be the supreme offering to the buddhas. During the future dreadful times Hearing one of these four-line verses And memorizing it will be an offering to all the buddhas. {58}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1316}} “They will always obtain the best provisions. They will always eat the best alms of the land. {{note:{index:526,id:UT22084-055-001-1317}}} As the best senior heirs of the one with ten strengths, They will for a long time make offerings to many jinas. {59}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1318}} “They will also see myself here on Vulture Peak Mountain. And I, in buddha wisdom, will thus prophesy to them. Also, after my passing away, there will be Maitreya, {{note:{index:527,id:UT22084-055-001-1319}}} Who at that time will also prophesy to them. {60}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1320}} “Similarly, Buddha Amitāyus also Has taught many other kinds of benefits: ‘All will enter my Sukhāvatī, And go to Abhirati and see Buddha Akṣobhya.’ {{note:{index:528,id:UT22084-055-001-1321}}} {61} {{page:{number:84,folio:F.43.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1322}} “For countless hundreds of thousands of eons They will never have the fear of downfalls. In this supreme practice of bodhisattva conduct They will always experience happiness. {62}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1323}} “In that way it has been taught that this, Which is preeminent, has the most excellent merit. May I learn every single word, And in future times be a keeper of this sūtra.” {{note:{index:529,id:UT22084-055-001-1324}}} {63}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1325}} Conclusion of the eleventh chapter, “Becoming a Keeper of the Sūtra.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1326}} “Young man, those are the qualities and benefits that bodhisattvas who know the nature of all phenomena will have. They will describe the true, excellent qualities of the tathāgatas. They will not falsely say that which is untrue about the tathāgatas. Why is that? It is because they know perfectly that nature, which is the nature through which a tathāgata comes to be. {{note:{index:530,id:UT22084-055-001-1327}}} They know the infinite qualities of a buddha. Why is that? Young man, the qualities of a buddha are infinite, inconceivable, beyond thought. They cannot be conceived or measured. Why is that? The mind, young man, is taught to be without a nature of its own, {{note:{index:531,id:UT22084-055-001-1328}}} to be without form. {{note:{index:532,id:UT22084-055-001-1329}}} Young man, that nature of the mind is also the nature of the qualities of a buddha. That nature of the qualities of a buddha is also the nature of the tathāgatas, and that is the nature of all phenomena.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1330}} “Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who know correctly that teaching on the nature of all the qualities are, young man, called bodhisattva mahāsattvas with profound comprehension. They are skilled in emancipation. They know perfectly emancipation from the three realms. They have perfect knowledge, do not teach that which is erroneous, and do not say that which is anything other than true. {{page:{number:85,folio:F.43.b}}} Their conduct is in line with what they teach. They have no attachment to the three realms. They have transcended the three realms. They have transcended the level of desire, the level of form, the level of formlessness, the level of the kleśas, the level of names, and the level of language. They are skilled in the way of letters and words. They know freedom from letters. {{note:{index:533,id:UT22084-055-001-1331}}} They have mastered the inexpressible Dharma. They know letters. They are skilled in letters. They are skilled in the knowledge of the categories of letters and words. They are skilled in the knowledge of the detailed categories of letters and words. They are skilled in the knowledge of the categories of all the words {{note:{index:534,id:UT22084-055-001-1332}}} of the Dharma. They are skilled in the knowledge of the detailed categories of all the words {{note:{index:535,id:UT22084-055-001-1333}}} of the Dharma. They are skilled in the knowledge {{note:{index:536,id:UT22084-055-001-1334}}} of the presentation of all the Dharma. They are endowed with the certainty of understanding, so that all the evil māras and all the devas in their entourages cannot overcome them.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1335}} At that time, when this Dharma teaching was given, ninety-eight times a hundred thousand million devas and human beings who had created the karma in previous lifetimes, {{note:{index:537,id:UT22084-055-001-1336}}} had accumulated {{note:{index:538,id:UT22084-055-001-1337}}} a trillion retentions, {{note:{index:539,id:UT22084-055-001-1338}}} were unobscured, and had insight into the Dharma, all attained patience. {{note:{index:540,id:UT22084-055-001-1339}}} The Bhagavān prophesied to them all that after four million, eight hundred thousand countless eons they would attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. He prophesied to each of them their separate names, their identical lifespans, and the individual buddha realms where they would attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.
It was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1341}} “The wise bodhisattvas who seek to attain The highest, supreme enlightenment, Who are skilled in meaning and the Dharma, Practice the nature of phenomena. {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1342}} “They say nothing that is untrue About the unique qualities of the buddhas. The heroes, free of all doubt, Know the nature of the jinas. {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1343}} “They know that all phenomena have but a single meaning, And that is solely emptiness. They do not have different meanings. They become adept in that single meaning. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1344}} “The wise know that they are without thought, Are devoid of thought, and that there is no object. {{page:{number:86,folio:F.44.a}}} They have eliminated without remainder Every conception of cessation and noncessation. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1345}} “They do not see the one with ten strengths as form, But see the lion of men as the dharmakāya. Neither do they conceive of attributes Because they have eliminated all error. {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1346}} “The qualities are inconceivable, beyond thought. They have the nature of complete peace. With this knowledge they thus see The buddhas as the supreme among humans. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1347}} “Just as they know their own conceptions to be, Thus they direct their understanding of everything. All phenomena have that nature, Which is as completely pure as space. {{note:{index:541,id:UT22084-055-001-1348}}} {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1349}} “Nothing arises to their conceptual mind. They know emancipation {{note:{index:542,id:UT22084-055-001-1350}}} from all phenomena. They are liberated from the three realms And they have no aspiration for them. {{note:{index:543,id:UT22084-055-001-1351}}} {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1352}} “They are those who see correctly and do not say Anything to the contrary or any untrue words. All the words that they speak Come forth through the power of the jinas. {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1353}} “They transcend the level of desire, And the levels of kleśas, form, and formlessness. Their minds have no attachment to phenomena. They practice with joy, benefiting beings. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1354}} “They have transcended the level of words; Their knowledge of language is obtained from its nature. For however long they speak They know those words have no basis. {11}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1355}} “There is no activity of conceptualization; Incorrect views have completely ceased. Their understanding is completely assured. It has a stability like that of space. {12}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1356}} “Even though quintillions of māras Come to disturb their mind, They overcome all the māras And do not fall under their power. {13}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1357}} “They have rejected the net of the māras. They have pure, untroubled conduct. They aspire to the bliss of dhyāna And know the world to be empty. {14}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1358}} “Even though it is said the world is an aggregate, They know it to be empty, And that all phenomena are like space, Without birth and without cessation. {15}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1359}} “They have forsaken the self, but not the conduct {{note:{index:544,id:UT22084-055-001-1360}}} Or listening to the teaching of the one with ten strengths. {{note:{index:545,id:UT22084-055-001-1361}}} {{page:{number:87,folio:F.44.b}}} They have attained perfect conduct And will be reborn wherever they pray to be. {16}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1362}} “They go to the buddha realms. They see many millions of buddhas. They have no desire for the deva realms And they do not pray to be there. {17}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1363}} “While they are practicing the Dharma, Their diligence does not waver for an instant. They are highly praised by The buddhas in the ten directions. {18}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1364}} “Therefore, young man, when you have received This Dharma teaching of the samādhi, Rejecting the profits of the intellect, Teach this Dharma to the people. {19}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1365}} “One who wishes for the numerous qualities Possessed by the self-arisen buddha Should train in this goodness And become a buddha with the ten strengths.” {20}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1366}} Conclusion of the twelfth chapter, “The Training According to the Samādhi.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1367}} Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should be skilled in teaching this samādhi.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1368}} “Young man, what is the teaching of this samādhi? It is the true nature of all phenomena; it is equality; it is the absence of inequality; it is devoid of notions; it is devoid of concepts; it is devoid of creation; it is devoid of arising; it is devoid of production; it is devoid of cessation; it is the termination of notions, concepts, and assumptions; it is devoid of an object for the mind; it is devoid of a focus of the mind; {{note:{index:546,id:UT22084-055-001-1369}}} it is the termination of designations; it is the termination of concepts from analysis; it is the termination of desire, anger, and ignorance; it is without a limited or limitless focus of the mind; it is the termination of any focus of the mind; it is the knowledge of the nature of the skandhas, dhātus, and āyatanas; it is the state of accomplishing the field of activity that is the performance of the conduct of mindfulness, understanding, comprehension, conscience, and stability; it is the level of freedom from corruptions; {{note:{index:547,id:UT22084-055-001-1370}}} it is the level of peace; it is the termination of all conceptual elaboration; it is the training of all bodhisattvas; it is the field of activity of all tathāgatas; {{page:{number:88,folio:F.45.a}}} and it is the perfection of all good qualities.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1371}} “Young man, that is what the teaching of samādhi is said to be. Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are established in this teaching of samādhi become inseparable from samādhi—their minds become free of delusion, they become endowed with great compassion, and they accomplish the benefit of countless beings.”
Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1373}} “The level of unequaled samādhi {{note:{index:548,id:UT22084-055-001-1374}}} Is peaceful, subtle, and difficult to see. All conceptions have been eliminated. Therefore it is called samādhi . {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1375}} “There are no notions, there are no concepts, There is nothing to be grasped, there is nothing to be shown, And there is no object for the mind. Therefore it is called samādhi . {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1376}} “When in a state of meditation There is no pride concerning any phenomenon. That very absence of pride— That is what is called samādhi . {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1377}} “There does not exist {{note:{index:549,id:UT22084-055-001-1378}}} even an atom of phenomena. That which is called ‘an atom’ does not exist. There are no phenomena as objects for the mind. Therefore it is called samādhi . {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1379}} “ ‘The mind has no object’ Is also itself a concept. When there are no concepts of phenomena, Then that is known as samādhi . {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1380}} “A word indicates a meaning. That word is not a thing. A word is like an echo, Like the space of the sky. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1381}} “These phenomena are not present; There is no presence to be perceived. The nonpresence is through the word ‘presence.’ Its nature is that there is nothing to be found. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1382}} “One says ‘going’ and ‘passing away,’ But that ‘going’ does not exist. Through the word ‘going’ there is the absence of going. That is given the name samādhi. {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1383}} “Saying ‘I am not meditating’ is called pride. {{note:{index:550,id:UT22084-055-001-1384}}} ‘I am meditating’ is a second kind of pride. {{note:{index:551,id:UT22084-055-001-1385}}} Practicing for enlightenment without pride, {{note:{index:552,id:UT22084-055-001-1386}}} And attaining {{note:{index:553,id:UT22084-055-001-1387}}} the absence of pride is the highest enlightenment. {{note:{index:554,id:UT22084-055-001-1388}}} {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1389}} “This unequaled equality is the level of peace; {{note:{index:555,id:UT22084-055-001-1390}}} It is śamatha and vipaśyanā, {{note:{index:556,id:UT22084-055-001-1391}}} devoid of attributes. Relying upon this peace, the level of buddhahood, Is engaging in the meditation {{note:{index:557,id:UT22084-055-001-1392}}} of samādhi. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1393}} “It is not possible through words to enter Into the understanding of the meaning. {{page:{number:89,folio:F.45.b}}} When all sounds and words are abandoned There will be meditation without pride. {11}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1394}} “When there is the fire of the eon’s end in this world That fire does not burn the supreme mountain in its center, Just like space that has never been burned in the past, Even though the fire burns for many hundreds of eons. {{note:{index:558,id:UT22084-055-001-1395}}} {12}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1396}} “The bodhisattvas who remain engaged In this samādhi as it has been taught, And know that phenomena are the same as space, Will also not be burned by fire. {{note:{index:559,id:UT22084-055-001-1397}}} {13}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1398}} “If the buddha realm were burning And in this samādhi they prayed For the burning to completely cease, Though the earth was destroyed it would be unchanged. {14}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1399}} “They will have infinite miraculous powers. They will travel through the air unimpeded. The bodhisattvas will have these qualities By remaining in samādhi just as they have been taught. {15}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1400}} “Though one is born and though one dies, There is no birth and there is no death. For the one who understands that This samādhi will not be difficult to attain. {16}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1401}} “The Lord of the World has taught That there is no death and there is no birth. Just as the Lord of the World knew that, You should also know it through this samādhi. {17}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1402}} “Unstained by the world, They have no attachment to worldly phenomena. With a body free of impediment They go to the buddha realms. {18}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1403}} “They constantly see in those realms The perfect buddhas, the guides of the world. They listen there to the Dharma That is taught in the realms of the buddhas. {{note:{index:560,id:UT22084-055-001-1404}}} {19}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1405}} “They will never be in ignorance. They will teach the essence of phenomena. They always know the way of phenomena, Which is composed {{note:{index:561,id:UT22084-055-001-1406}}} of the essence of phenomena. {20}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1407}} “Even though they teach for ten million eons, Their confidence in speech will not decline. They emanate many other bodhisattvas Who have wisdom. {21}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1408}} “The emanated bodhisattvas Travel from realm to realm. They are seated, cross-legged, Upon lotuses that have a thousand petals. {22}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1409}} “They teach the enlightenment of buddhahood, Wonderful dhāraṇīs and sūtras, {{page:{number:90,folio:F.46.a}}} And ten million other sūtras, While meditating peacefully in samādhi. {23}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1410}} “They establish in irreversibility Countless multitudes of beings, And teach the enlightenment of buddhahood Without their confidence in speech ever declining. {24}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1411}} “They go to a pinnacled hall That is adorned with jewels And scatter aromatic Flowers upon the guides. {25}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1412}} “They also sprinkle scented Powders upon the guides. They all make vast offerings In order to attain enlightenment. {26}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1413}} “Those countless qualities Are the refuge of the bodhisattvas. When they are free of kleśas They attain those miraculous powers. {27}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1414}} “Because the kleśas are not created They are clear, pure, and bright. The field of activity of the bodhisattvas Is noncomposite and inviolate. {28}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1415}} “They have perfect peace, complete peace; They have no kleśas, and they have no misery. {{note:{index:562,id:UT22084-055-001-1416}}} They have no conceptualization, are free of conceptualization, And have transcended conceptualization. {29}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1417}} “This characteristic of phenomena Is beyond the scope of words. {{note:{index:563,id:UT22084-055-001-1418}}} It is difficult {{note:{index:564,id:UT22084-055-001-1419}}} to know through language {{note:{index:565,id:UT22084-055-001-1420}}} And therefore it is called samādhi . {30}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1421}} “It is unending; it is complete peace; It is effortless, and it cannot be shown. The field of activity of all the buddhas Is the completely pure summit of the truth. {31}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1422}} “The training of all the buddhas Is in the nature of all phenomena. The perfect buddhas, having trained in it, Have reached the perfection of qualities. {{note:{index:566,id:UT22084-055-001-1423}}} {32}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1424}} “Without any concepts of the past, Of this side and the further side, In that way all those buddhas Have reached the perfection {{note:{index:567,id:UT22084-055-001-1425}}} of qualities. {33}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1426}} “Knowing the nature of phenomena As having no coming or going, They have reached the perfection That is nonconceptual and effortless.” {34}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1427}} Conclusion of the thirteenth chapter, “The Teaching of the Samādhi.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1428}} Then the youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, {{page:{number:91,folio:F.46.b}}} with palms placed together he bowed toward the Bhagavān and said to him, {{note:{index:568,id:UT22084-055-001-1429}}} “Bhagavān, it is marvelous that the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha has taught the equality that is the nature of all phenomena, which is the samādhi that all bodhisattvas train in.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1430}} “Bhagavān, it was thus, in this training, that the Bhagavān trained for a long time, and accomplished the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. Bhagavān, that gives me confidence to speak. {{note:{index:569,id:UT22084-055-001-1431}}} Sugata, it gives me confidence to speak.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1432}} The Bhagavān said, “Young man, if you think the time has come, be confident to speak.”
Since the Bhagavān had granted the youth Candraprabha this opportunity, Candraprabha spoke the following verses of praise directly to the Bhagavān.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1434}} “You saw beings tormented by suffering, {{note:{index:570,id:UT22084-055-001-1435}}} Constantly overpowered by desire and anger, And developed the aspiration to attain enlightenment: ‘May I become a buddha who liberates beings!’ {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1436}} “Hero, {{note:{index:571,id:UT22084-055-001-1437}}} for many millions of eons, constantly, You practiced generosity, self-restraint and self-control, Patience, correct conduct, and similarly diligence, And your acts of generosity were vast and infinite. {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1438}} “Without ever any sadness in your mind You gave away your legs, arms, and even your life, And similarly, without attachment you gave away Gold, silver, sons, wives, and your kingdom. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1439}} “Your conduct was stainless and pure. You made a gift of yourself without ruining your conduct. You controlled well your body, speech, and mind. Sugata who has a self-restrained mind, I pay homage to you. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1440}} “Delighting in patience, residing on the path of patience, Even though your body was cut into pieces you were not angered; {{note:{index:572,id:UT22084-055-001-1441}}} Through your meditation on love, milk flowed from you. Marvelous Sugata, I pay homage to you. {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1442}} “You possess the strength of the ten strengths. With wisdom free of attachment you know all phenomena. {{page:{number:92,folio:F.47.a}}} With compassion, Lord of Dharma, you benefit the world. Through your kindness you wish to benefit beings. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1443}} “You know emptiness and that there are no such beings, And likewise you see that the world’s beings have lost that path. You have realized that the nature of phenomena is selfless And that though you bring beings to liberation, there is no such liberation. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1444}} “With discrimination you reject all carelessness. You have conquered the infinite, powerful māras. Enlightened at buddhahood, you have vast, infinite wisdom. You teach the supreme Dharma of completely pure peace. {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1445}} “The sky with its moon and the stars may fall, The earth with its mountains and towns may be destroyed, The element of space may change into something else, But you will never speak an untrue word. {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1446}} “You have seen the suffering of beings Who take joy in the perception of objects. You teach the profound peace, emptiness, In which there is no perception of objects. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1447}} “Great hero, you trained For countless millions of eons In the training of nonperception, And so you are free of error. {11}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1448}} “Just as you have trained in the Dharma, In that way you teach the Dharma. Yours is not the level of foolish beings, And neither is it the level of all the tīrthikas. {12}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1449}} “Those who have the conception of a self, They are unwise beings who are in error. You know that phenomena have no self, And so you are free of any error. {13}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1450}} “You speak the truth, great hero; You are established in the true Dharma. Lord, you remain within truth, within veracity, And you speak words that are true. {14}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1451}} “Your conduct has been true, Just as you have prayed for. You have the consequence of that true conduct And you speak words that are true. {15}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1452}} “You have perfected true conduct. You have trained in the summit of truth. You have truly practiced with a true motivation. I pay homage to you who have true wisdom. {16}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1453}} “There is no equal to your wisdom. Your words of wisdom illuminate. You have attained unique wisdom. I pay homage to you who speak words of wisdom. {17}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1454}} “You have meditated on kindness And become a friend to all beings. {{page:{number:93,folio:F.47.b}}} You are as unshakable as Sumeru. You are completely stable and unwavering. {18}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1455}} “Teacher, your following is vast. You have attracted these followers. Sugata who has profound wisdom, Make your voice resound within this assembly. {19}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1456}} “The voice of the Buddha is a lion’s roar. You walk with the gait of a lion. You defeat all the tīrthikas Like a lion defeats jackals. {20}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1457}} “Hero who subdues the unsubdued, The unsubdued are subdued by you. They become friends who are reliable, Inseparable, and pleasant to be with. {21}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1458}} “You see the beings who are suffering Because they maintain the view of a self. {{note:{index:573,id:UT22084-055-001-1459}}} You teach the Dharma of no-self In which there is neither like nor dislike. {22}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1460}} “The foolish who are untrained Take up the wrong paths. You show them the path That the guides have followed. {23}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1461}} “Whoever holds to the concept of a self, They will remain in suffering. They do not know selflessness, Within which there is no suffering. {24}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1462}} “You teach the Dharma with words that are without error. Lord of the World, you make no error. You are one who speaks words that are never incorrect. I pay homage to you, who bring freedom from suffering. {25}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1463}} “In the sky there are many quintillions Of devas, nāgas, and yakṣas. They all feel joy in the Guide When they hear the meaningful words of the Bhagavān. {26}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1464}} “Your words are mild, gentle, and pleasing, Timely, melodious, appropriate, and beloved. You have the countless qualities of speech That benefit and bring liberation to many beings. {27}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1465}} “Countless hundreds of thousands of musical instruments Are all played melodiously and simultaneously, But the Sugata with one word eclipses them all With his unique, divine, beloved voice. {{note:{index:574,id:UT22084-055-001-1466}}} {28}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1467}} “Avadavats {{note:{index:575,id:UT22084-055-001-1468}}} and flocks of birds {{note:{index:576,id:UT22084-055-001-1469}}} with beautiful songs, With their beautiful songs that are pleasing to everyone— All of the songs of these many flocks of birds {{note:{index:577,id:UT22084-055-001-1470}}} Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. {29} {{page:{number:94,folio:F.48.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1471}} “Deva maidens with beautiful voices And with melodious music and songs, And the sound of lutes, paṭaha {{note:{index:578,id:UT22084-055-001-1472}}} drums, bherī drums, {{note:{index:579,id:UT22084-055-001-1473}}} and conches, Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. {{note:{index:580,id:UT22084-055-001-1474}}} {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1475}} “The songs of cuckoos, parrots, and mynas, Of cranes, peacocks, and kiṃnaras— All these beautiful, melodious sounds Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. {{note:{index:581,id:UT22084-055-001-1476}}} {30}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1477}} “Delightful, melodious, beautiful, enjoyable, Exquisite, peaceful voices singing praises— All such voices singing simultaneously Are not as delightful as the Tathāgata’s perfect speech. {31}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1478}} “The light from all luminous beings, From devas, {{note:{index:582,id:UT22084-055-001-1479}}} humans, kings, and asuras, {{note:{index:583,id:UT22084-055-001-1480}}} And from all beings in the three existences, Are eclipsed by one light ray from the Sugata. {32}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1481}} “The Sugata’s body is like a blossomed flower With the various adornments of all the special signs. A pure and clear accomplishment of hundreds of merits, The body of the Jina shines on the entire world. {33}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1482}} “The sound of conches and of paṇavas, {{note:{index:584,id:UT22084-055-001-1483}}} And the sound of bherī drums {{note:{index:585,id:UT22084-055-001-1484}}} and kimpalas {{note:{index:586,id:UT22084-055-001-1485}}} — All those beautiful and delightful sounds Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. {34}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1486}} “The sounds of quintillions of musical instruments, Clear and beautiful voices like those of the devas, {{note:{index:587,id:UT22084-055-001-1487}}} And the delightful voices of male and female devas {{note:{index:588,id:UT22084-055-001-1488}}} Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. {{note:{index:589,id:UT22084-055-001-1489}}} {35}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1490}} “Flocks of a multitude of birds—cranes, peacocks, Shelducks, cuckoos, geese, and snipe— May simultaneously sing their songs, but they Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. {{note:{index:590,id:UT22084-055-001-1491}}} {36}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1492}} “The voices of nāgas, yakṣas, asuras, mahoragas, Devendra, {{note:{index:591,id:UT22084-055-001-1493}}} Brahmā, and the lords of the devas— All the lovely and beautiful voices in the three existences Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. {37}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1494}} “The light of Brahmā and lords of the devas, The light of the sun and precious jewels, The many different kinds of light— All those lights are eclipsed by the brilliance of the Jina’s light. {{note:{index:592,id:UT22084-055-001-1495}}} {38}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1496}} “Your body, speech, and mind are perfectly pure. The purity of your wisdom is unstained by the three existences. {{page:{number:95,folio:F.48.b}}} Lord of men, you have the wealth of qualities, precious qualities. Self-arisen one, through all your qualities, you are without equal.” {39}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1497}} In that way the youth spoke those words with great joy, Praising the one with ten strengths, the speaker of truth. He said, “By offering to the measureless, {{note:{index:593,id:UT22084-055-001-1498}}} unquantifiable Buddha May I also become a buddha like Śākyamuni!” {40}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1499}} Knowing his perfect conduct, the Sugata, The Lord of humans, the one with wisdom free of attachment, smiled. Maitreya, the senior son of the one with ten strengths, asked him, “For what reason did the Guide smile? {41}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1500}} “The earth has shaken in six ways. The devas and nāgas in the sky are filled with joy. They are gazing at the Buddha with great delight and happiness. I pray to the unconquerable Sugata that you elucidate this to them. {42}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1501}} “You have a supreme being’s wisdom, Which is not the level of the Bhagavān’s śrāvakas. You who have pure wisdom beyond examples, wise one, Tell {{note:{index:594,id:UT22084-055-001-1502}}} us the entire reason, Jina, why you smiled. {{note:{index:595,id:UT22084-055-001-1503}}} {43}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1504}} “You are the Śākya lion, possessor of the ten strengths, the Guide, The chief of humans, the one who has reached the perfection of wisdom. {{note:{index:596,id:UT22084-055-001-1505}}} You have eliminated intractable desire, anger, and ignorance. To you who shine with intense light, I ask this question: {44}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1506}} “Seeking the supreme, highest enlightenment, You, the Guide, practiced for millions of eons As numerous as the grains of sand in the Ganges. For what reason did you show a smile? {45}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1507}} “Seeking the supreme, highest enlightenment, You, the Teacher, gave away your arms and legs. You gave away sons, wives, companions, and relations. Sage, for what reason did you show a smile? {46}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1508}} “You gave away horses, elephants, and chariots, {{note:{index:597,id:UT22084-055-001-1509}}} Slaves, jewels, silver, and pearls. {{note:{index:598,id:UT22084-055-001-1510}}} When you practiced the sublime conduct There were no jewels or wealth that you did not give away. {47}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1511}} “You have the supreme wisdom in the three existences. You know the conduct of all beings. {{page:{number:96,folio:F.49.a}}} You are skilled in knowing their natures, minds, and aspirations. For what reason did you smile? {48}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1512}} “Who made the offering to you, best of men? For whom has vast merit been created? Who has gained that excellent conduct? Sage, for what reason did you smile? {49}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1513}} “The earth has shaken in six ways. Millions of lotuses have appeared on the ground. {{note:{index:599,id:UT22084-055-001-1514}}} They shine and have millions of excellent petals. They are the color of gold, beautiful and delightful. {50}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1515}} “Present here are the heart sons of the Jina Who show the greatest bodhisattva miracles. Many {{note:{index:600,id:UT22084-055-001-1516}}} dharmabhāṇakas have gathered here. Guide, I ask my question for their sake. {51}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-1517}} “The sound of bherī drums, {{note:{index:601,id:UT22084-055-001-1518}}} conches, and gongs, {{note:{index:602,id:UT22084-055-001-1519}}} Of quintillions of instruments has resounded.
