{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2485}} “I rejoice in those who live in the forest, Always alone and solitary like a rhinoceros, Always with pure livelihood and few activities, Without acting hypocritically for the sake of reputation. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2486}} “I rejoice in those who have no entanglements, Who have no envy or yearning for a home, Who are always terrified of the three realms And act without attachment to the world. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2487}} “I rejoice in those who are without complication And are saddened by every rebirth into existence. This samādhi will not be difficult to attain For those who do not dispute but have peaceful minds. {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2488}} “I rejoice in those who see the harmfulness of crowds, Who avoid every kind of disagreement, Who live in solitude, dwelling at the foot of trees, And who are heirs of the sugatas focused upon liberation. {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2489}} “I rejoice in those who live in solitude, Neither praising themselves nor criticizing others. I rejoice in those who are not careless But careful in the Buddha’s teaching. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2490}} “That carefulness is the very root Of all the qualities of the aspects of enlightenment. This samādhi is not difficult to attain For any heirs of the Buddha who are always careful. {11}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2491}} “The teaching of the Sugata is a treasure that has been found. Attaining homelessness is a second treasure. The attainment of faith is a third treasure. This samādhi is a fourth treasure. {12}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2492}} “On learning of emptiness, of the field of activity of the buddhas, If it is not rejected, that is a treasure that has been found. Endless eloquence is a treasure that has been found, And any dhāraṇī is a supreme treasure. {13}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2493}} “That carefulness is the very root Of all the virtuous qualities that have been proclaimed, And of correct conduct, learning, giving, and patience. The Sugata has taught that it is a treasure that has been found. {14}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2494}} “For those who are careful in the Buddha’s teaching, For those who have perfect aspirations, {{page:{number:174,folio:F.88.a}}} This samādhi will not be difficult to obtain. They are established in the Buddha’s teaching.” {15}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2495}} Conclusion of the twenty-sixth chapter, “Rejoicing.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2496}} Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, as it has been said, ‘Be careful,’ you, young man, should consequently train in that way. Why is that? Because, young man, for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are careful, the highest, complete enlightenment is not difficult to attain, let alone this samādhi.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2497}} “Young man, in what way should bodhisattva mahāsattvas be careful? For that, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas should have perfectly pure conduct. Young man, in what way should bodhisattva mahāsattvas have perfectly pure conduct? For that, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have perfectly pure conduct, never separating from an all-knowing mind, should practice the six perfections. Listen, for I shall teach you their benefits.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2498}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who aspire to generosity. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] the kleśa of avarice is overcome; [2] their minds are constantly devoted to generosity; [3] from the ordinary wealth of the populace they obtain what is essential; [4] they are reborn into a wealthy family, and as soon as they are born they have a mind that aspires to generosity; {{note:{index:886,id:UT22084-055-001-2499}}} [5] they are beloved by the fourfold assembly; [6] they enter the assembly without fear or lack of confidence; [7] verses that praise their greatness spread to the cardinal and intermediate directions; [8] they have soft and youthful arms and legs; [9] they stand on feet with level soles; {{note:{index:887,id:UT22084-055-001-2500}}} and [10] they are never apart from kalyāṇamitras {{note:{index:888,id:UT22084-055-001-2501}}} until they are seated at the Bodhimaṇḍa. {{page:{number:175,folio:F.88.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2502}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who aspire to generosity.”
It was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2504}} “Avarice is overcome. Their generosity increases. They are those who obtain the essentials And are reborn into a wealthy family. {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2505}} “As soon as they are born There is generosity in their minds. They are beloved by beings, Both the laity and mendicants. {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2506}} “They enter the assembly Fearlessly and confidently. Their renown spreads Through the villages and towns. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2507}} “They have soft arms and legs That they gain without difficulty. They obtain kalyāṇamitras, Both buddhas and śrāvakas. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2508}} “They never have an avaricious mind; Their minds always delight in generosity. They are beloved by millions of beings. Those are the benefits of being without avarice. {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2509}} “They are reborn into a family with great wealth. At birth they have minds that delight in generosity. They obtain the essentials and choose the time of passing away. Those are the benefits of being without avarice. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2510}} “Fearlessly they enter an assembly. Their renown spreads in all directions. They always have soft arms and legs. Those are the benefits of being without avarice. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2511}} “It is not difficult for them to obtain kalyāṇamitras. They also see buddhas and śrāvakas. Seeing them, they make offerings to them with faith. Those are the benefits of being without avarice.” {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2512}} Conclusion of the twenty-seventh chapter, “The Benefits of Generosity.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2513}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from perfectly pure, correct conduct. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they devote {{note:{index:889,id:UT22084-055-001-2514}}} themselves to wisdom and perfect it; [2] they follow the example of the buddhas; [3] they do not criticize the wise; [4] they do not waver from their vows; [5] they maintain their practice; [6] they turn away {{note:{index:890,id:UT22084-055-001-2515}}} from saṃsāra; [7] they are led to attain nirvāṇa; {{note:{index:891,id:UT22084-055-001-2516}}} [8] they live without faults arising; {{page:{number:176,folio:F.89.a}}} [9] they attain samādhi; and [10] they will never be poor. {{note:{index:892,id:UT22084-055-001-2517}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2518}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have perfectly pure, correct conduct.”
It was said concerning this:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2520}} “They bring wisdom to perfection, Follow the example of the buddhas, Do not criticize those who are wise, And they are always without fear. {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2521}} “They do not waver from their vows, They maintain their practice, They are led to attain nirvāṇa, And they turn away from saṃsāra. {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2522}} “They live without faults arising, They quickly attain samādhi, They will not be poor, And they maintain correct conduct. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2523}} “Their wisdom will be perfected, And they follow the example of the buddhas. They never make criticisms of the wise, And thus their conduct is completely pure. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2524}} “The wise ones never waver from their vows. The heroic ones {{note:{index:893,id:UT22084-055-001-2525}}} maintain their practice. Seeing the many faults of saṃsāra They go toward nirvāṇa. {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2526}} “There are no faults {{note:{index:894,id:UT22084-055-001-2527}}} that arise in their minds; Thus, they maintain the strength of correct conduct, And quickly attain an immaculate {{note:{index:895,id:UT22084-055-001-2528}}} samādhi. Those are the benefits of pure, correct conduct.” {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2529}} Conclusion of the twenty-eighth chapter, “The Teaching on Correct Conduct.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2530}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from maintaining patience and being kind. {{page:{number:177,folio:F.89.b}}} What are these ten? They are: [1] they are not burned by fire; [2] they are not slain by weapons; [3] they are not affected by poison; [4] they do not drown in water; [5] the devas protect them; [6] they attain a body adorned by the primary signs of a great being; [7] all the doorways to their rebirth in lower existences are closed; [8] it is not difficult for them to be reborn in the paradise of Brahmā; [9] they are happy day and night; and [10] their physical sensations of comfort and pleasure are never lost.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2531}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from maintaining patience and being kind.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2533}} “They are not burned by fire, They are not killed by weapons, They are not affected by poison, They do not drown in water, {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2534}} “They are protected by devas, They have the thirty-two primary signs, And the lower existences are closed to them. Those are the benefits of patience. {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2535}} “The state of Brahmā and the state of Śakra Are not difficult for them to attain. They always dwell in happiness And have inconceivable pleasure. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2536}} “They are not slain by fire or weapons; They are not killed by poison or drowning. They are protected by devas, nāgas, and yakṣas. Those are the benefits of maintaining kindness. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2537}} “Their bodies will have the thirty-two primary signs. They will not fall into the lower existences, And at death they will be reborn in the realm of Brahmā. Those are the benefits of maintaining patience. {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2538}} “They have happiness day and night. Their bodies will have pleasurable sensations. They will have the power of patience and bliss. Those wise ones will always have a tranquil mind. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2539}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from taking up diligence. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] it is difficult to approach their level; {{note:{index:896,id:UT22084-055-001-2540}}} [2] they attain the state of being cared for by the buddhas; [3] they will be cared for by the devas; [4] they maintain the Dharma they have received; [5] they obtain the Dharma they have not previously received; [6] they attain the lineage of samādhis; {{note:{index:897,id:UT22084-055-001-2541}}} [7] they have few illnesses; [8] they digest their food well; [9] they are like lotuses; and [10] they are not like pestles. {{note:{index:898,id:UT22084-055-001-2542}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2543}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from taking up diligence.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2545}} “It is difficult to approach their level. {{note:{index:899,id:UT22084-055-001-2546}}} They are without idleness. {{note:{index:900,id:UT22084-055-001-2547}}} The devas protect them. They quickly {{note:{index:901,id:UT22084-055-001-2548}}} see the buddhas. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2549}} “Their prayers are fulfilled, {{note:{index:902,id:UT22084-055-001-2550}}} They attain the lineage of samādhis, And they do not become ill. {{note:{index:903,id:UT22084-055-001-2551}}} {{page:{number:178,folio:F.90.a}}} Those are the benefits of diligence. {{note:{index:904,id:UT22084-055-001-2552}}} {8–9} {{note:{index:905,id:UT22084-055-001-2553}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2554}} “They digest pleasurably, without harm, That which they eat and drink. {10} They gradually develop Like a blue lotus in the middle of water. {{note:{index:906,id:UT22084-055-001-2555}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2556}} “In that way the bodhisattvas Develop through good qualities. {11} The days and the nights Pass fruitfully for them. {{note:{index:907,id:UT22084-055-001-2557}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2558}} “The Tathāgata who has engaged in diligence, Gaining accomplishments for numerous eons, Has taught to the bodhisattvas These benefits of possessing diligence. {12}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2559}} “Those who engage in diligence Are in the care of the jinas. The devas, too, make aspirations for them. They will soon attain the Buddha’s enlightenment. {13}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2560}} “What they have learned will never diminish, And they give many other Dharma teachings. Their confidence of speech increases immensely. Those are the benefits of engaging in diligence. {14}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2561}} “They will quickly attain the lineage of samādhis. They will never become ill. Whatever food they eat They will comfortably digest completely. {15}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2562}} “Day and night the good qualities Of their powerful diligence increase. Through the power of this diligence, Before long they will attain enlightenment. {16}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2563}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from being devoted to meditation. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they maintain their bodhisattva conduct; [2] they engage in the field of that conduct; {{note:{index:908,id:UT22084-055-001-2564}}} [3] they live free from anguish; [4] their sensory faculties are protected; {{note:{index:909,id:UT22084-055-001-2565}}} [5] they experience pleasure; {{note:{index:910,id:UT22084-055-001-2566}}} [6] they are separated from desire; [7] they have insatiability for meditation; [8] they are free from the domain of Māra ; [9] they are established in the domain of the Buddha; and [10] they ripen the state of liberation.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2567}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from being devoted to meditation.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2569}} “They are never without bodhisattva conduct, As they are established in bodhisattva conduct. The yogins practice the field of that conduct, And reject that which is not the field of that conduct. {17}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2570}} “They live without anguish. Their senses hidden and bound, They experience pleasure. {{page:{number:179,folio:F.90.b}}} Their field of conduct is practicing meditation. {18}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2571}} “They are without desire, or the craving of desire. They abide in the bliss of meditation. They are free from the domain of Māra And dwell in the Buddha’s domain. {19}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2572}} “This is the particular quality of the yogins: That they delight in being alone in the forest. They bring liberation to fruition. Those are the ten aspects. {20}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2573}} “The bodhisattvas remain in bodhisattva conduct And they reject everything that is not that conduct. They reject that which is not the field of that conduct and remain in that which is. Those are the benefits of endeavoring in samādhi. {21}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2574}} “They never experience anguish. They reach the state of higher bliss. Both their body and mind become blissful. These are the benefits of endeavoring in meditation. {{note:{index:911,id:UT22084-055-001-2575}}} {22}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2576}} “They live secretly in solitary places. They never have any distractions. Thus their bodies are in isolation And they attain happiness free of desires. {23}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2577}} “They are unstained by desires and have no kleśas. Thus they are free from the domain of Māra And are established in the domain of the tathāgatas. They bring their liberation to fruition. {24}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2578}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from engaging in wisdom. What are these ten? They are: [1] they give away all their possessions without becoming proud that they are pure; [2] they have immaculate, correct conduct without forming an attachment to that conduct; [3] they maintain the power of patience without maintaining the conceptualization that there are beings; [4] they take up diligence in isolation from body and mind; {{note:{index:912,id:UT22084-055-001-2579}}} [5] in meditating they meditate with a non-abiding meditation; [6] they are invincible to the māras; [7] they are unshakable to all adversaries; {{note:{index:913,id:UT22084-055-001-2580}}} [8] they attain illumination regarding all engagement with the composite; {{note:{index:914,id:UT22084-055-001-2581}}} [9] they engage in vast great compassion for all beings, and have no aspiration for the level of the śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas; {{note:{index:915,id:UT22084-055-001-2582}}} {{page:{number:180,folio:F.91.a}}} and [10] they enter into the dhyānas, samādhis, and samāpattis of the buddhas. {{note:{index:916,id:UT22084-055-001-2583}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2584}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from engaging in wisdom.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2586}} “The heroic ones give away all their possessions But do not become proud that they are pure. They keep their correct conduct immaculate But they form no attachment to that. {25}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2587}} “The wise ones meditate on patience But have expelled the conceptualization of beings. They are those who engage in diligence But in isolation from body and mind. {26}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2588}} “They are those who cultivate meditation, But without abiding and independent; They are invincible to the māras. Those are the qualities of those who have wisdom. {27}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2589}} “They are unshakable To every adversary And have obtained the illumination of saṃsāra. Those are the qualities of wisdom. {28}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2590}} “They have attained great compassion Toward all beings. They never have an aspiration For the wisdom of the śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha. {29}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2591}} “They are not proud of being pure through giving away all their possessions. They have immaculate correct conduct but have no attachment to conduct. They meditate on patience but have no conceptualization of beings. Those are the benefits of being devoted to wisdom. {30}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2592}} “They engage in diligence but in isolation. {{note:{index:917,id:UT22084-055-001-2593}}} They meditate without being bound, without fixation. They are wise {{note:{index:918,id:UT22084-055-001-2594}}} and are invincible to Māra. {{note:{index:919,id:UT22084-055-001-2595}}} Those are the benefits of being devoted to wisdom. {31}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2596}} “They are unshakable to adversaries. {{note:{index:920,id:UT22084-055-001-2597}}} They have discovered the shallowness {{note:{index:921,id:UT22084-055-001-2598}}} of the composite, And they have vast compassion for beings. Those are the benefits of being devoted to wisdom. {32}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2599}} “They never give rise to an aspiration to be A pratyekabuddha or śrāvaka, And thus they are established in the qualities of a buddha. Those are the benefits of being devoted to wisdom. {{note:{index:922,id:UT22084-055-001-2600}}} {33}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2601}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from becoming very learned. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they do not create kleśas; {{note:{index:923,id:UT22084-055-001-2602}}} [2] they do not develop malice; {{note:{index:924,id:UT22084-055-001-2603}}} {{page:{number:181,folio:F.91.b}}} [3] they expose doubts; [4] they make views accurate; [5] they shun the wrong paths; [6] they are established on the true path; [7] they have reached the doorway to deathlessness; [8] they are close to enlightenment; [9] they are a light for beings; and [10] they have no fear of the lower existences.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2604}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from becoming very learned.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2606}} “These are taught to be the ten benefits From becoming very learned Just as they are known By the Tathāgata, the Buddha. {34}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2607}} “They know the two aspects Of the kleśas and of purification. They reject the kleśas And follow {{note:{index:925,id:UT22084-055-001-2608}}} the path of purification. {35}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2609}} “The wise ones reject doubts And develop accurate views. They shun the wrong path And follow the correct path. {36}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2610}} “They are at the door to deathlessness And they are close to enlightenment. They are a light for beings And they are not afraid of the lower existences. {37}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2611}} “They know the numerous properties of having the kleśas, And in the same way they know the aspect of purification. They completely reject the kleśas And train in the supreme quality of purification. {38}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2612}} “They expose the doubts of all beings. They have a view that is always accurate. They shun the wrong path And are always upon the true path of peace. {39}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2613}} “They are always beside the doorway to deathlessness; They are always close to stainless enlightenment. They have become a light to all the multitudes of beings And they have no fear of the lower existences. {40}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2614}} “Young man, for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are intent on giving the Dharma, there are ten benefits that come from giving the Dharma. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they reject that which should not be done; [2] they engage in that which should be done; [3] they follow the Dharma of a worthy person; [4] they purify buddha realms; [5] they reach the Bodhimaṇḍa; [6] they give away material things; [7] they overcome the kleśas; {{page:{number:182,folio:F.92.a}}} [8] they give their portion {{note:{index:926,id:UT22084-055-001-2615}}} to all beings; [9] they meditate on love toward those on whom their minds are focused; and [10] they attain happiness in this life.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2616}} “Young man, for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are intent on giving the Dharma, those are the ten benefits that come from giving the Dharma.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2618}} “Those who give the supreme gift, The gift of the Dharma, are not misers. The Lord of the World has taught That they will have ten benefits. {41}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2619}} “They reject all that should not be done; The wise ones engage in what should be done. They obtain the Dharma of a worthy person And maintain a motivation of generosity. {42}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2620}} “They purify a buddha realm. {{note:{index:927,id:UT22084-055-001-2621}}} Their realm is inconceivable. {{note:{index:928,id:UT22084-055-001-2622}}} They are always on the Bodhimaṇḍa, {{note:{index:929,id:UT22084-055-001-2623}}} Which is the result of giving the Dharma. {43}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2624}} “They give away all material things. They follow the king of the Dharma. For those who have overcome the kleśas, Enlightenment is not hard to attain. {44}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2625}} “With a loving mind they give Their portion to all beings. They are those who have no envy, And they have a happiness higher than that of humans. {45}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2626}} “They are learned people who reject what should not be done. They are wise people who are always doing what should be done. They always follow the Dharma of great beings. They are learned people who always give the gift of the Dharma. {46}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2627}} “Their realm is one that is always pure. They increase those qualities that are aspects of enlightenment. They are always close to the Bodhimaṇḍa. Those are the benefits of giving the Dharma. {47}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2628}} “They have no kleśas, and give material things away. They know the characteristics of things. They are liberated from all attachment. They never have any impediments. {48}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2629}} “They have a wise one’s mind. They wish for all beings to be happy. They have loving minds free of envy, And in this life their happiness is not little. {49}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2630}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who dwell in emptiness. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they dwell in the dwelling of the Buddha; {{note:{index:930,id:UT22084-055-001-2631}}} {{page:{number:183,folio:F.92.b}}} [2] their meditation is nondwelling; {{note:{index:931,id:UT22084-055-001-2632}}} [3] they are not intent on rebirth; {{note:{index:932,id:UT22084-055-001-2633}}} [4] they have no clinging to conduct; {{note:{index:933,id:UT22084-055-001-2634}}} [5] they do not criticize superior beings; [6] they live in an appropriate manner; [7] they do not conceptualize the objects of perception; {{note:{index:934,id:UT22084-055-001-2635}}} [8] they remain detached; {{note:{index:935,id:UT22084-055-001-2636}}} [9] they do not disparage the buddhas; {{note:{index:936,id:UT22084-055-001-2637}}} and [10] they possess the Dharma. {{note:{index:937,id:UT22084-055-001-2638}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2639}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who dwell in emptiness.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2641}} “The yogins dwell in that which is The dwelling of the lords of men And the field of activity of all the buddhas, Without the conception of a life. {50}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2642}} “Without dependence on any existence They never give up the superior dhyāna. Having seen the nature of phenomena They have no intention of being reborn. {51}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2643}} “Those who have no clinging to conduct Will not be dependent on conduct. {{note:{index:938,id:UT22084-055-001-2644}}} They do not criticize in any way Another superior being {{note:{index:939,id:UT22084-055-001-2645}}} who is without defilement. {{note:{index:940,id:UT22084-055-001-2646}}} {52}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2647}} “They live in an appropriate manner And are not known to quarrel. The yogins do not conceptualize things But live always detached. {53}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2648}} “They do not disparage the Buddha Even for the sake of their life. While remaining in the emptiness of phenomena They are fearlessly visible in their body. {54}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2649}} “They teach the Dharma with veneration For the inconceivable enlightenment of buddhahood Of all the lords of the worlds, And they have no doubt in the Dharma of the Buddha. {55}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2650}} “The dwelling place of the supreme individuals, The level not that of the many kinds of tīrthika, There where there is no being, soul, or person: That is where the bodhisattvas dwell. {{note:{index:941,id:UT22084-055-001-2651}}} {56}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2652}} “They have no dwelling whatsoever. They remain in the bliss of nondwelling dhyāna. {{note:{index:942,id:UT22084-055-001-2653}}} They see that phenomena have no self, no being, And they do not give rise to the concept of creation. {57}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2654}} “They understand the nature of phenomena. They have no dependence even on conduct. They do not conceive of themselves as pure because of conduct, And always have faith in the buddhas. {{note:{index:943,id:UT22084-055-001-2655}}} {58}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2656}} “They meditate on the empty nature of all phenomena And they are never in any way inappropriate. {{page:{number:184,folio:F.93.a}}} They possess the pure Dharma of the tathāgatas And do not disparage the guides. {59}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2657}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who remain intently in meditative seclusion. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] their minds are unpolluted; [2] they remain careful; [3] they keep the Buddha in mind; [4] they have faith in bodhisattva conduct; {{note:{index:944,id:UT22084-055-001-2658}}} [5] they have no uncertainty concerning wisdom; {{note:{index:945,id:UT22084-055-001-2659}}} [6] they have gratitude toward the buddhas; {{note:{index:946,id:UT22084-055-001-2660}}} [7] they do not abandon {{note:{index:947,id:UT22084-055-001-2661}}} the Dharma; [8] they maintain vows perfectly; [9] they have attained the level of self-discipline; and [10] they have the direct perception of the four discernments.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2662}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who remain intently in meditative seclusion.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2664}} “Their minds are unpolluted. They have rejected all carelessness. They maintain carefulness. Their field of activity is meditative seclusion. {60}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2665}} “They have faith in the buddhas, having heard Of the conduct of the Lord of the World. The yogins have no doubt concerning wisdom, The inconceivable wisdom of the buddhas. {61}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2666}} “They have gratitude toward the buddhas, And have no doubt concerning the Dharma of the buddhas. They maintain their vows perfectly, And have attained the level of self-discipline. {62}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2667}} “They have attained discernment. They delight in being alone in the forest. They have forsaken gain and honors, And their field of activity is meditative seclusion. {63}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2668}} “Their minds are unpolluted. They have forsaken all carelessness. They are great beings who are always careful. Those are the benefits of being dedicated to samādhi. {64}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2669}} “They keep in mind the buddhas, the supreme humans, And they have faith in their supreme conduct. They do not doubt the wisdom of the tathāgatas. Those are the benefits of being dedicated to samādhi. {65}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2670}} “They always have gratitude toward the buddhas. They do not forsake the Dharma even for the sake of their life. At all times they keep their vows perfectly. Those are the benefits of being dedicated to samādhi. {66}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2671}} “They have attained the level of self-discipline. {{page:{number:185,folio:F.93.b}}} They quickly attain the direct perception of discernment. They speak with the unceasing confidence of speech. They teach millions and billions of sūtras. {67}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2672}} “They quickly attain the enlightenment of buddhahood. They protect the teaching of the Guide. They defeat all who are adversaries. They extensively propagate the enlightenment of buddhahood. {68}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2673}} “When those bodhisattvas pass away, They go to the realm of Sukhāvatī. They hear the highest Dharma from Amitāyus And attain the acceptance of the nonorigination of phenomena. {69}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2674}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are dedicated to solitude. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they have few activities; [2] they have gone far from busy crowds; [3] they have no quarrels; [4] they have no harm; [5] they do not increase defilements; {{note:{index:948,id:UT22084-055-001-2675}}} [6] they do not create any cause for disputes; [7] they have perfectly peaceful conduct; [8] they maintain perfect self-restraint; [9] their minds are prepared for liberation; and [10] they quickly manifest liberation.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2676}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are dedicated to solitude.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2678}} “They always have few activities. They have gone far from busy crowds. They have no quarrels. They live alone in the forest. {70}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2679}} “Without an intention to cause harm They do not increase their defilements. They have no cause for disputes. Those are the qualities of living in a forest. {71}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2680}} “They are peaceful in their conduct. They restrain their body, speech, and mind. They are prepared for liberation; They will quickly reach liberation. {72}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2681}} “They are yogins who always have few activities. They have shunned the many faults of busy gatherings. The yogins {{note:{index:949,id:UT22084-055-001-2682}}} do not ever quarrel. Those are the qualities of living in a solitary place. {73}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2683}} “When they have become saddened by the composite, They never harbor any longing for the world, And they do not increase their defilements. The ones who live in a forest gain these benefits. {74}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2684}} “There never arises in them a cause for disputes. {{page:{number:186,folio:F.94.a}}} They live in solitude, delighting in peace. Their body, speech, and mind are restrained. The ones who live in solitude will have many qualities. {75}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2685}} “They are prepared for liberation. They will quickly attain the peace of liberation. They dwell in the forest and are close to liberation. Those who dwell in solitude will have all these qualities. {76}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2686}} “Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who live by receiving alms in the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they have no desire for a reputation; [2] they have no desire for fame; [3] they have no desire for honors or gains; [4] they remain within the four noble families; {{note:{index:950,id:UT22084-055-001-2687}}} [5] they have no hypocrisy or boasting; [6] they do not praise themselves; [7] they do not criticize others; [8] they engage with households without aversion or attachment; {{note:{index:951,id:UT22084-055-001-2688}}} [9] they give the Dharma without expectation of a reward; {{note:{index:952,id:UT22084-055-001-2689}}} and [10] the Dharma they teach while remaining in the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy will be remembered.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2690}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who live by receiving alms in the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2692}} “They have no desire for a reputation. They do not wish for fame. Those who remain in the disciplines of mendicancy Are indifferent to gain and loss. {77}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2693}} “They do not abandon the noble family. They have no hypocrisy or boastfulness. They do not praise themselves And they do not criticize others. {78}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2694}} “They have no attachment or aversion, And teach the Dharma with no thought of reward. The words they speak will be remembered. Recipients of alms will have those qualities. {{note:{index:953,id:UT22084-055-001-2695}}} {79}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2696}} “They do not seek reputation, fame, or gain. They remain within the four noble families. The wise ones are neither hypocritical nor boastful. Those are the qualities of dedication to mendicancy. {80}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2697}} “They do not praise themselves or criticize others. They are not upset when spoken to harshly. They are not delighted when they hear themselves praised. {{page:{number:187,folio:F.94.b}}} Recipients of alms will have that contentment. {{note:{index:954,id:UT22084-055-001-2698}}} {81}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2699}} “They give the gift of the Dharma without thought of reward. They do not search for fame or gain. The words they speak will be remembered. Those are the benefits that come from dedication to mendicancy. {82}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2700}} “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who dwell in solitude while maintaining those qualities of the Dharma will obtain the treasure of the buddhas, they will obtain the treasure of the Dharma, they will obtain the treasure of wisdom, and they will obtain the treasure of knowing the past, the future, and the present.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2701}} “Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of the buddhas? Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who practice alone, who dwell in solitude, will attain the five higher cognitions. What are the five higher cognitions? They are divine sight, divine hearing, the knowledge of others’ minds, remembering past lives, and possessing miraculous powers. Young man, those are the five higher cognitions that are obtained. Through divine vision, which transcends human vision, the countless, innumerable buddha bhagavāns in the eastern direction are seen. In the same way the countless, innumerable buddha bhagavāns in the southern, western, and northern directions are seen. They constantly have this vision of the buddhas. Young man, in that way the bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of the buddhas.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2702}} “Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of the Dharma? The bodhisattva mahāsattvas hear with their divine hearing the Dharma that is taught by those buddha bhagavāns in the ten directions. They are constantly hearing the Dharma. Young man, in that way the bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of the Dharma.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2703}} “Young man, how do the bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of wisdom? Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have that wisdom obtain the entire Dharma. They do not forget anything that they have obtained, and teach the Dharma to beings, {{page:{number:188,folio:F.95.a}}} knowing what will be beneficial for any one person. Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of wisdom.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2704}} “Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of knowing the past, the future, and the present? Through the higher cognitions they gain the knowledge of the minds and conduct of all beings in the past, the future, and the present. Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of knowing the past, the future, and the present.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2705}} “Young man, in brief, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who maintain the qualities of the Dharma in that way will obtain the entire Dharma of the buddhas. This level is not reached by śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, let alone any adversary of the Dharma.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2707}} “The wise ones who remain in solitude Will quickly attain the treasure of the buddhas, The treasure of the Dharma, the treasure of wisdom, The treasure of the past, and the five higher cognitions.” {{note:{index:955,id:UT22084-055-001-2708}}} {83}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2709}} Conclusion of the twenty-ninth chapter, “Ten Benefits.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2710}} Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, you should train in this way, thinking, ‘I will abandon even the pleasures of the kingship of a divine cakravartin and enter homelessness.’
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2711}} “Young man, having entered homelessness you should maintain the disciplines of mendicancy, live in solitude, and develop perfect mildness and patience.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2712}} “Young man, you should apply yourself diligently, as if your hair and clothes were on fire, and listen to the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena , learn it, understand it, keep it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others.
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2713}} “Young man, you should always, like a rhinoceros, dwell without a companion in the forest.” {{note:{index:956,id:UT22084-055-001-2714}}} {{page:{number:189,folio:F.95.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2715}} Thereupon the Bhagavān, in order to explain this topic, {{note:{index:957,id:UT22084-055-001-2716}}} gave a detailed teaching on this episode from the past by chanting the following verses to the youth Candraprabha:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2717}} “I remember many hundreds of eons ago There was a guide of limitless renown. Multitudes of humans, devas, and nāgas made offerings to him. He was a jina named Tejaguṇarāja. {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2718}} “During that time there formed a community Of a hundred and sixty million bhikṣus with higher cognitions, Who had completely attained the power of the discernments, Who practiced the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy, and who had peaceful minds. {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2719}} “At that time there were in this Jambudvīpa One billion seven hundred and sixty million towns, And each of them was five yojanas wide, And was particularly supreme, made of the seven precious materials. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2720}} “At that time, all of those perfect towns Were adorned by many hundreds of parks, And all those parks were adorned With fresh flowers and fruit, like massed clouds. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2721}} “Those perfect parks were adorned With various beautiful trees with edible fruits— Covered with jackfruits, mangos, rose apples, and breadfruit, And with hundreds of karnikara, magnolia, and puṇṇaga trees. {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2722}} “At that time, flocks of birds in banyan trees would sing— Hundreds of cuckoos, avadavats, and peacocks, And flocks of many other birds were heard: The songs of parrots, {{note:{index:958,id:UT22084-055-001-2723}}} partridges, and snipes. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2724}} “There was the supreme sound of the songs of bees and partridges That equaled that of Dhṛtarāṣṭra, {{note:{index:959,id:UT22084-055-001-2725}}} the king of geese. They had bright, multicolored bodies, brilliant with great hues, And sang delightful, beautiful, charming songs. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2726}} “At that time, there were gatherings of these birds, There were the songs of avadavats, peacocks, and parrots, {{note:{index:960,id:UT22084-055-001-2727}}} Cuckoos, mynas, and a variety of other birds— Various kinds of songs from many birds. {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2728}} “They dwelt in those hundreds of parks Where there were the blossoms of karnikara, Gardenia, aśoka, and kachnar trees, As well as red lotuses, blue lotuses, night lotuses, and white lotuses. {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2729}} “They were beautified by lotus flower ponds That were adorned by a hundred thousand lotuses. There were beautiful, exquisite lotus ponds {{page:{number:190,folio:F.96.a}}} Adorned by the fragrance of the most delightful scents. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2730}} “At that time, the king in this Jambudvīpa Was the lord of men whose name was Dṛdhadatta. He had five hundred sons Who were handsome and beautiful to see. {11}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2731}} “At that time the kingdom was peaceful and happy, Free of calamities, and filled with joy and peace. Jambudvīpa was adorned by many flowers. It was identical to a paradise, with no difference. {12}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2732}} “At that time there was a jina, one with the ten strengths, Without bad actions, who taught this supreme samādhi: ‘The beings within existence are like dreams. There is no one who is born and no one who dies. {13}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2733}} “ ‘There is no being to be found, and no soul, {{note:{index:961,id:UT22084-055-001-2734}}} or person. {{note:{index:962,id:UT22084-055-001-2735}}} These phenomena are like dreams {{note:{index:963,id:UT22084-055-001-2736}}} or a plantain tree; {{note:{index:964,id:UT22084-055-001-2737}}} Like illusions, the same as lightning in the sky; Like the moon on water, the same as a mirage. {{note:{index:965,id:UT22084-055-001-2738}}} {14}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2739}} “ ‘There is no person who dies in this world, Who departs and goes to another world. But the karma that has been created is not destroyed. It will ripen as good and bad results within saṃsāra. {15}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2740}} “ ‘It is neither eternal nor is it annihilated. There is no accumulation or presence of karma, Yet if it has been created there is no way to avoid encountering it, While that which is created by others will not be experienced. {16}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2741}} “ ‘There is no passing away or returning. There is no existence of all things, yet neither are they nonexistent. There is no pure engagement with the locus of a view. There is no conduct of beings and no engagement with peace. {17}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2742}} “ ‘The conduct of the sugatas, the qualities of the jinas, Are birthlessness, peace, and the absence of attributes. The supreme leaders, the buddhas, have these strengths and retentions, And the strength of the ten strengths. {18}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2743}} “ ‘The supreme good qualities, the accumulation of qualities, Are the supreme qualities, wisdom, retentions, strengths, The supreme manifestation of miraculous powers, And the attainment of the five {{note:{index:966,id:UT22084-055-001-2744}}} supreme higher cognitions. {19}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2745}} “ ‘There is no essence here to be known whatsoever. There is no coming, no going; that is the subtle {{note:{index:967,id:UT22084-055-001-2746}}} mode of phenomena. {{note:{index:968,id:UT22084-055-001-2747}}} The essence of phenomena has no movement whatsoever, Thus the mode of phenomena is the mode of no movement. {20}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2748}} “ ‘The natural mode is not in the accumulation of words. This mode, this nature, does not dwell anywhere. {{page:{number:191,folio:F.96.b}}} The natural mode is without dwelling, is nondependent. It is the level of peace, the stainless domain of the jinas. {21}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2749}} “ ‘It is the mode of peace, complete peace, total peace. That mode does not dwell anywhere. It always accompanies the nature of things. It is subtle, {{note:{index:969,id:UT22084-055-001-2750}}} difficult to see, and an unfluctuating state. {22}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2751}} “ ‘It does not fluctuate but continues to be itself. It is a continuing nature that neither stays nor comes. This continuing nature cannot be described. It is the empty, unfluctuating continuity of phenomena. {23}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2752}} “ ‘It is taught in words but it is not the mode of words. The mode of the nature of words is the mode of phenomena. The aggregation of words has no location anywhere, And that mode of its nature is the mode of phenomena. {24}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2753}} “ ‘The words that describe the mode are not the mode of being. The nature of phenomena is a mode of subtle {{note:{index:970,id:UT22084-055-001-2754}}} meaning. Though words are spoken, that is not the mode of being; Words cannot be found and neither can the mode of being. {25}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2755}} “ ‘There is no endlessness, nor an end, nor a mode in between. There is no existence nor nonexistence, nor a partial mode. The knowledge of that mode of nature Is the same in the teachings of all the supreme jinas. {26}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2756}} “ ‘The stainless, pure, ultimate state— Peace, complete peace, without stain, free of stain— There are no concepts or pride in the state of peace That is taught by the Jina, the one with perfect compassion. {27}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2757}} “ ‘In this there is no usage of letters. It is a vast mode, a vast mode of meaning. The buddhas honor it; the jinas praise it. The appearance of the Dharma is a subtle mode. {28}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2758}} “ ‘The unequaled sugatas remain in that Stainless, vast treasure of the Dharma. They teach the stainless, precious Dharma, The ultimate truth of emptiness, the subtle {{note:{index:971,id:UT22084-055-001-2759}}} mode of meaning.’ {{note:{index:972,id:UT22084-055-001-2760}}} {29}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2761}} “When King Dṛdhadatta heard That the supreme human was teaching this samādhi, He then {{note:{index:973,id:UT22084-055-001-2762}}} came into the presence of the compassionate Jina Accompanied by eighty quintillion others. {30}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2763}} “The sovereign over men felt veneration for the Jina Who was endowed with the strengths, and bowed down to his feet. While he stayed in front of the one with the ten strengths, Filled with joy, he placed his ten fingers together in homage. {31}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2764}} “The Jina, who was perfect, with control over his senses, Perceived the king’s pure conduct. {{page:{number:192,folio:F.97.a}}} The supreme human knew his aspiration And taught him this supreme samādhi. {32}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2765}} “When the king had heard this ultimate truth He experienced a vast, superior joy. He gave up all of the four continents. He abandoned pleasures and left his home. {33}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2766}} “When the king gave up the world and entered homelessness For the sake of enlightenment and to become a jina, All the people in this Jambudvīpa {{note:{index:974,id:UT22084-055-001-2767}}} Gave up all sensory pleasures and entered homelessness too. {34}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2768}} “At that time there was a vast assembly with the ten strengths. There were many diligent bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs. At that time, herbs grew without ploughing, And devas came to serve and attend to them. {35}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2769}} “The three orange Dharma robes manifested, Perfectly cut and sewn, without parallel, Unsullied, stainless, adorned, beautifully golden, Arising from the Buddha’s qualities and the power of merit. {36}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2770}} “See, young man, look how that supreme king Gave up the entire world and entered homelessness. {{note:{index:975,id:UT22084-055-001-2771}}} In the age of destruction there will be many beings Who will have few possessions but will not leave their homes. {{note:{index:976,id:UT22084-055-001-2772}}} {37}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2773}} “There will be many in chains and suffering punishments, Who are abused, threatened, and have unwished-for suffering. There will be many who will have to endure harm from royal families, {{note:{index:977,id:UT22084-055-001-2774}}} Who will have very few possessions and no food in their homes. {38}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2775}} “They will have very short lives and no wealth. They will be very careless and have no power of merit. They will be stupid, and unskilled in any craft. They will be in poverty with nothing in their homes. {39}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2776}} “They will be impure and desire the wives of others. They will be envious and extremely rash. They will be degenerate and behave badly— Yet they will say, ‘I am going to be a buddha.’ {{note:{index:978,id:UT22084-055-001-2777}}} {40}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2778}} “They will make deceptive promises and be brazen, saying, ‘I am wealthy and I will give the wealth of the Dharma to the world.’ {{note:{index:979,id:UT22084-055-001-2779}}} They will cause harm, be hypocritical and dishonest— Yet they will say, ‘I am going to be a buddha.’ {41}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2780}} “They will delight in killing, binding, and attacking others; They will have bad conduct, and be cruel and aggressive. They will have no gratitude, be divisive and violent— {{page:{number:193,folio:F.97.b}}} Yet will say, ‘I am a noble practitioner of bodhisattva conduct.’ {42}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2781}} “They will become angry with anyone Who they hear teaching bodhisattva conduct. When they hear something that is stupid {{note:{index:980,id:UT22084-055-001-2782}}} and mistaken They will repeat those blameworthy words a hundred times. {{note:{index:981,id:UT22084-055-001-2783}}} {43}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2784}} “Young man, having heard these words of mine, Do not follow {{note:{index:982,id:UT22084-055-001-2785}}} those others. If you wish to reach the highest enlightenment They are not to be trusted, even in a dream. {44}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2786}} “One could recount for hundreds of eons the many qualities Ascribed to the austere disciplines of mendicancy, But without possessing those qualities One will not attain the peace of the highest enlightenment. {45}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2787}} “Always be good and gentle. Always have pure conduct and a serene mind. Continually maintain pure conduct, And before long you will attain the supreme samādhi. {46}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2788}} “Do not be proud and do not be harsh. Always have a mind that is serene. Eliminate all pride, arrogance, and hiding of your faults, And attain this supreme samādhi. {47}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2789}} “Always remember the Jina’s qualities. The color of perfect gold, shining brightly, Like the sky at night filled with stars: The Sage’s body is filled with signs. {48}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2790}} “The descendant of Manu who remembers the moon of the Sage While walking, sitting, standing, or lying down Will always have the Teacher present before him, And he will have vast happiness. {{note:{index:983,id:UT22084-055-001-2791}}} {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2792}} “Holding many powders and ointments, And excellent parasols, banners, canopies, and flags, Always make offerings to the Sugata And this supreme samādhi will soon be attained. {49}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2793}} “Holding many musical instruments And excellent, exquisite {{note:{index:984,id:UT22084-055-001-2794}}} incense, garlands, and flowers, Make offerings always to the Jina’s stūpas And this supreme samādhi will soon be attained. {50}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2795}} “With many kinds of excellent songs and dance, With amusements and performances made with a pure mind, With excellent lights and incense, Always make excellent offerings to the unequaled one. {{note:{index:985,id:UT22084-055-001-2796}}} {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2797}} “With hundreds of paṇava drums and loud mṛdaṅga drums, With paṭaha drums, lutes, {{note:{index:986,id:UT22084-055-001-2798}}} the excellent sound of flutes, {{page:{number:194,folio:F.98.a}}} With the qualities of music of various kinds of melodious sounds, Make an offering to the Guide with a pure mind. {51}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2799}} “Create beautiful images of the Buddha, Perfectly made of precious materials, {{note:{index:987,id:UT22084-055-001-2800}}} That are attractive and extremely beautiful, And this supreme samādhi will soon be attained. {52}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2801}} “Make excellent images that are fashioned From gold or silver, and also sandalwood, That are attractive and extremely beautiful, And this supreme samādhi will soon be attained. {{note:{index:988,id:UT22084-055-001-2802}}} {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2803}} “Make images that are fashioned of clay, Or stone, or wood, or painted, That are attractive and extremely beautiful, And this supreme samādhi will soon be attained. {{note:{index:989,id:UT22084-055-001-2804}}} {ii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2805}} “Always remain in the solitude of forests, Forsaking the joys of villages and towns. Be without a companion, like a rhinoceros, And this supreme samādhi will soon be attained. {53}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2806}} “I am the Lord of the Dharma; you are my son. Train in this samādhi practice of mine. I was at that time Dṛdhadatta, the world-renowned Ruler over the descendants of Manu. {{note:{index:990,id:UT22084-055-001-2807}}} {54}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2808}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I made offerings to countless buddhas in the past. I always maintained pure conduct And I honored those with the ten strengths. {{note:{index:991,id:UT22084-055-001-2809}}} {55}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2810}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, In the past I gave up my sons and wives. I gave away my supreme, excellent head, legs, Arms, and eyes without ever being disheartened. {56}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2811}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I gave away wealth and grain, Hundreds of male and female slaves, and many jewels, And satisfied numerous beggars. {57}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2812}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, In the past I gave away great quantities Of pearls, crystals, gold, conches, ammonite stones, {{note:{index:992,id:UT22084-055-001-2813}}} beryls, Perfectly pure jewels, and a mass {{note:{index:993,id:UT22084-055-001-2814}}} of coral, {58}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2815}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I gave away vast amounts of excellent jewelry Of various kinds, such as perfect strings of pearls, Lion jewelry, {{note:{index:994,id:UT22084-055-001-2816}}} and nets of jewels. {59} {{page:{number:195,folio:F.98.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2817}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, In the past I gave away many millions Of fine, excellent clothes that were perfectly clean, Made of the finest silk and cloth and beautified by gold threads. {60}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2818}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I gave away various kinds of elephants, horses, chariots, And my own beloved sons and women, Without ever experiencing any unhappiness. {61}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2819}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, Whenever I saw people who were very poor, Who were in distress and suffering because of their need, I freed them from their poverty. {62}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2820}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I have in the past given to beggars Trillions of {{note:{index:995,id:UT22084-055-001-2821}}} horses, elephants, and chariots Draped in nets of precious jewel adornments. {63}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2822}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I have in the past joyfully and with compassion Given away many trillions Of excellently decorated parks. {64}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2823}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I have in the past given away beautifully adorned Villages, towns, regions, and market towns, And having given them felt continuous joy. {65}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2824}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I have in the past given to those who requested them Heaps of jewels as large as Sumeru And a similar amount of clothes and adornments. {66}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2825}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I have made those who are very poor rich, I have protected those who were in great distress, And I have made happy many who were enduring suffering. {67}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2826}} “When I was a sovereign over this world And saw the suffering of the population, I felt compassion and wished them to be happy, And gave my kingdom to them. {68}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2827}} “Young man, the marvelous things that I have done, And the hardships I have undergone for many hundreds of eons, I would not be able to complete recounting them Even in a quintillion eons. {69}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2828}} “Seeking this peace, this supreme samādhi, I underwent astonishing hardships. The people without faith in the Sugata’s conduct Will have minds that become crazed and polluted. {70}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2829}} “Young man, I declare this to you: {{page:{number:196,folio:F.99.a}}} Have faith in me; my words are not untrue. The Sugata does not speak words that are false. The compassionate Jina always speaks the truth. {71}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2830}} “These many different kinds of practices I will have carried out for many {{note:{index:996,id:UT22084-055-001-2831}}} eons. {{note:{index:997,id:UT22084-055-001-2832}}} However I attain this supreme samādhi I will then free millions of beings from suffering. {{note:{index:998,id:UT22084-055-001-2833}}} {72}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2834}} “In the moment that I have attained This samādhi, the path of great wisdom, Having attained this supreme samādhi I will see numerous millions of buddhas. {73}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2835}} “I will have attained infinite miraculous powers, And my emanations will go to hundreds of realms, And there I will ask the compassionate ones Many quintillions of questions. {74}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2836}} “The sugatas will give me answers For my quintillions of questions, And having obtained them I will remember them all And I will not forget even a single word. {75}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2837}} “Having listened to the answers to those Quintillions of correct questions, I will teach the stainless state of peace And establish many beings on the path of wisdom. {76}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2838}} “I will remain in this samādhi And train in it for many hundreds of eons, And will first bring many quintillions of beings On to the highest stainless path. {77}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2839}} “Those who have not seen the previous sugatas Who have taught this stainless way Will not be able to have faith In the supreme samādhi of emptiness, the ultimate truth. {78}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2840}} “The people who have faith, are wise, and know the practice, Are always joyful when they hear The way that is correct and profound, And do not become frightened or terrified. {79}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2841}} “They hold the supreme enlightenment. They have been reborn as my sons. They are like fig-tree flowers, And I practice for hundreds of eons for their sake. {80}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2842}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Have no fear of falling into unfortunate existences, Are always free of the eight disadvantageous states, And will see numerous millions of buddhas. {81}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2843}} “They who have this supreme samādhi in their hands, {{page:{number:197,folio:F.99.b}}} I prophesy, will have unending understanding, And like the kind Jina {{note:{index:999,id:UT22084-055-001-2844}}} who has infinite fame, {{note:{index:1000,id:UT22084-055-001-2845}}} They will accomplish many benefits for beings. {82}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2846}} “They who possess this samādhi Will have understanding and memory, High wisdom, will retain what they have heard, And will possess vast confidence of speech. {83}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2847}} “They who possess this samādhi Will receive the offerings of devas, Will be continually revered by humans, {{note:{index:1001,id:UT22084-055-001-2848}}} And will be constantly protected by the hosts of spirits. {{note:{index:1002,id:UT22084-055-001-2849}}} {84}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2850}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Do not die in fire or water, Are not harmed by poison or weapons, And cannot be reached by enemies. {85}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2851}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will always dwell in forest bowers, Where they will be constantly attended by devas, And where many yakṣas will be their servants. {86}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2852}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will have wisdom that is as vast as the ocean, Will describe without impediment the qualities of the Sage, And make known correctly the qualities of the Buddha. {87}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2853}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will have endless, boundless learning That is beyond measure, like space, And will hold the torch of wisdom that dispels darkness. {88}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2854}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will always be gentle, will speak appropriate words, Will be beloved in the midst of their followers, And their speech will be like the lion’s roar. {89}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2855}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will be like healing physicians, The support, protector, and refuge of many, And will bring illumination to the worlds. {90}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2856}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will not take pleasure in sexual intercourse. {{note:{index:1003,id:UT22084-055-001-2857}}} They will enjoy śamatha and reach the bliss of dhyāna. With a peaceful voice {{note:{index:1004,id:UT22084-055-001-2858}}} they will speak of peace. {91}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2859}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will not take pleasure in conceptualization, Will be free of the entire multitude of concepts, And those wise ones will constantly be in meditation. {{page:{number:198,folio:F.100.a}}} {92}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2860}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will attain extraordinary vision And will see the infinite jinas. They will be leaders with infinite sight. {93}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2861}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will have the sweet and melodious voice of a crane, {{note:{index:1005,id:UT22084-055-001-2862}}} The sound of the avadavat and a drumbeat, {{note:{index:1006,id:UT22084-055-001-2863}}} And a singing sound and gentle voice. {94}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2864}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will have a voice that is like resounding thunder. Their gentle speech will be like the song of a goose And their voice will have the fifty aspects of speech. {{note:{index:1007,id:UT22084-055-001-2865}}} {95}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2866}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will speak with an inconceivable voice That has the pleasant sound of the various aspects of speech For numerous quintillions of eons. {96}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2867}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will not have attachment to food, Will not delight in alms bowls or dharma robes, But with few desires they will be content and abstinent. {97}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2868}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Do not praise themselves And never criticize others. They always delight in dhyāna and have a subtle mind. {98}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2869}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Always examine themselves, Do not look for mistakes in others, And the entire world does not impede them. {99}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2870}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Have pure conduct and untroubled minds, Are never deceitful or dishonest, Are always gentle, and always delight in liberation. {100}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2871}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Are always motivated to generosity, Take no delight in avarice, And always have correct conduct. {101}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2872}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Are handsome, good looking, and attractive. Their bodies shine like the purest gold And have the thirty-two primary signs of a great being. {102}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2873}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Always have an attractive appearance, Are observed and beloved by many people, {{page:{number:199,folio:F.100.b}}} And those people never have enough of gazing upon them. {103}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2874}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Always delight, gladden, and enchant Devas, nāgas, and likewise the yakṣas, Who enter towns {{note:{index:1008,id:UT22084-055-001-2875}}} and praise them. {{note:{index:1009,id:UT22084-055-001-2876}}} {104}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2877}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Always have Brahmā, Śakra, and many powerful deities Acting as their attendants, But there is no pride in their minds. {105}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2878}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Have no fear of the lower existences. They have no fear of the disadvantageous existences or bad rebirths. They are completely free of all fear of bad rebirths. {106}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2879}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Have no doubts or uncertainties On hearing in detail the supreme Dharma of the Buddha, And they follow that profound wisdom. {107}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2880}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi, Whatever subtle Dharma teachings they hear They attain perfect mastery of them all, And gain their power and detailed reasoning. {108}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2881}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Constantly think, ‘I will always act in accordance With what the Jina’s words have taught,’ And attain unique, supreme retention. {109}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2882}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Will, when the time of their death comes, Have before them the compassionate Amitābha And his host of bhikṣus. {{note:{index:1010,id:UT22084-055-001-2883}}} {110}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2884}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Are those who have attained the retentions, Have perfect mastery over the treasure of the Dharma, And possess the unceasing words of eloquence. {111}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2885}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi, With peaceful conduct and peaceful {{note:{index:1011,id:UT22084-055-001-2886}}} minds Will be an illumination for beings Wherever those holders of the Dharma go. {{note:{index:1012,id:UT22084-055-001-2887}}} {112}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2888}} “They attain the ten bhūmis: {{note:{index:1013,id:UT22084-055-001-2889}}} Perfect Joy, Stainless, Shining, Brilliance , Difficult to Master, Manifest, Gone Far, Unwavering, Perfect Understanding , and Clouds of Dharma. {{note:{index:1014,id:UT22084-055-001-2890}}} {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2891}} “Those heroes attain the ten powers: {{note:{index:1015,id:UT22084-055-001-2892}}} Life, {{note:{index:1016,id:UT22084-055-001-2893}}} karma, {{note:{index:1017,id:UT22084-055-001-2894}}} materials, {{note:{index:1018,id:UT22084-055-001-2895}}} and devotion, {{note:{index:1019,id:UT22084-055-001-2896}}} And the strengths of aspiration, {{note:{index:1020,id:UT22084-055-001-2897}}} miracles, {{note:{index:1021,id:UT22084-055-001-2898}}} and birth, {{note:{index:1022,id:UT22084-055-001-2899}}} {{page:{number:200,folio:F.101.a}}} Dharma, {{note:{index:1023,id:UT22084-055-001-2900}}} mind, {{note:{index:1024,id:UT22084-055-001-2901}}} and likewise great wisdom. {{note:{index:1025,id:UT22084-055-001-2902}}} {ii}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2903}} “They who possess this supreme samādhi Are skilled in the various aspects of the supreme Dharma treasure, Have attained the perfect power of the dharmakāya, And cut through the doubts of all beings. {{note:{index:1026,id:UT22084-055-001-2904}}} {113}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2905}} “If all beings were compassionate bhagavāns, And were sugatas until existence comes to an end, And if someone were to make offerings to them for many hundreds of eons Or for more eons than there are sand grains in the Ganges, {114}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2906}} “And if in this latter time of destruction Someone were to hear this samādhi And say only the words ‘I rejoice in this!’ The previous merit would not be a fraction of this accumulation. {115}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2907}} “Young man, whoever has this practice of peace, This supreme samādhi, the ultimate truth of emptiness, Propagates it and creates copies of it, That one is a dharmabhāṇaka with wisdom.” {116}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2908}} Conclusion of the thirtieth chapter, “Tejaguṇarāja.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2909}} Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who think, ‘I shall understand the languages of all beings and, knowing their higher or lesser capabilities, I will teach them the Dharma,’ those bodhisattva mahāsattvas should listen to the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena , learn it, understand it, keep it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others.”
Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2911}} “They who, desiring liberation, possess this stainless samādhi See the countless guides of the past, Ask those lords of the world about their previous practice, And those bodhisattvas dwell in supreme roots of merit. {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2912}} “They who, desiring liberation, possess this stainless samādhi Obtain the highest happiness of devas and humans, {{page:{number:201,folio:F.101.b}}} Obtain the supreme offerings of devas and humans, And obtain the happiness of dhyāna, the supreme, noble happiness. {{note:{index:1027,id:UT22084-055-001-2913}}} {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2914}} “They who, desiring liberation, possess this stainless samādhi Do not become thrilled on hearing the highest praises, Do not become saddened by being criticized, And like a mountain are unmoved by the eight worldly concerns. {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2915}} “They who, desiring liberation, possess this stainless samādhi Speak perfectly {{note:{index:1028,id:UT22084-055-001-2916}}} pleasantly, with gentle words, Do not frown, always speak sincerely, Have a smiling face, and have been instructed by the guides. {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2917}} “They who, desiring liberation, possess this stainless samādhi Are pleasant, good company, have a gentle mind, Are always restrained {{note:{index:1029,id:UT22084-055-001-2918}}} and established in self-discipline, And are very gentle, have pleasing speech, {{note:{index:1030,id:UT22084-055-001-2919}}} and speak tenderly. {{note:{index:1031,id:UT22084-055-001-2920}}} {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2921}} “They who, desiring liberation, possess this stainless samādhi Do not quarrel or cause conflict when they speak. They have freed themselves from all stubbornness {{note:{index:1032,id:UT22084-055-001-2922}}} and anger And are always joyful, {{note:{index:1033,id:UT22084-055-001-2923}}} pleasant, and gentle. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2924}} “They who, desiring liberation, possess this stainless samādhi Are always wise and are constantly motivated to generosity. When they see beings in great suffering they give them their food; They delight in giving to others, and not in their own enjoyment. {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2925}} “They who, desiring liberation, possess this stainless samādhi Are admired by a hundred thousand devas, Are always attended by nāgas, asuras, and yakṣas, And are protected by those who dwell in the forest and its environs. {{note:{index:1034,id:UT22084-055-001-2926}}} {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2927}} “They speak with unimpeded words, like the voice of Brahmā, Have a voice like the song of a goose, a voice like a kiṃnara’s song, {{note:{index:1035,id:UT22084-055-001-2928}}} Have the fifty aspects of speech and have a sound that brings joy, {{note:{index:1036,id:UT22084-055-001-2929}}} And have a resounding voice, a proclaiming voice, a perfect voice. {{note:{index:1037,id:UT22084-055-001-2930}}} {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2931}} “Even if someone knew how to reduce All the worlds into their smallest particles, They who possess this supreme, stainless samādhi Would voice sounds that were even more numerous. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2932}} “They who possess this stainless samādhi Attain the ten powers, and attain the eight and two bhūmis. The wise ones attain the inconceivable qualities of a buddha, {{page:{number:202,folio:F.102.a}}} Subjugate all māras, and reach the highest enlightenment.” {{note:{index:1038,id:UT22084-055-001-2933}}} {i}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2934}} Conclusion of the thirty-first chapter, “Benefits.”
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2935}} Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wonder, ‘How can I know the nature of all phenomena?’ should listen to this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena , learn it, understand it, keep it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others.”
Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2937}} “In the ones who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena No desire arises, no anger arises, Nor in those great leaders does ignorance ever arise. They have eliminated all kleśas without remainder. {1}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2938}} “They who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena Are heart children of the Sugata who do not abandon the training. They are heroes who never fall under the power of women. Everywhere they rejoice in the teaching of the sugatas. {2}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2939}} “They who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena Are wise, sagacious, and know the way of wisdom. {{note:{index:1039,id:UT22084-055-001-2940}}} They see infinite, endless buddhas And know infinite dhāraṇīs {{note:{index:1040,id:UT22084-055-001-2941}}} and wisdom. {{note:{index:1041,id:UT22084-055-001-2942}}} {3}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2943}} “They who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena Will before long become a lord of humans. They know the skills of healing and bestow happiness, {{note:{index:1042,id:UT22084-055-001-2944}}} And they are able to remove all the pain of suffering. {{note:{index:1043,id:UT22084-055-001-2945}}} {4}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2946}} “They who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena Know that sentient beings are suffering. They always beat the drum of the elixir. They will before long become a guide. {{note:{index:1044,id:UT22084-055-001-2947}}} {5}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2948}} “They are the supreme physicians, skilled in healing. They know the origin of all illnesses and how to be freed from them. {{page:{number:203,folio:F.102.b}}} They have wisdom and train correctly. Having trained they liberate many lost beings. {6}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2949}} “They who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena Are wise heroes who are skilled in the nature of emptiness. They have no attachment to the world and always their food is alms, And they bring many beings to supreme enlightenment. {{note:{index:1045,id:UT22084-055-001-2950}}} {7}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2951}} “They who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena {{note:{index:1046,id:UT22084-055-001-2952}}} Are moons {{note:{index:1047,id:UT22084-055-001-2953}}} among people, superior through the power of patience. They are not angry even if struck with stones and sticks, And they are not disturbed even if their limbs are severed. {8}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2954}} “They who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena Have the strength of being established in the strength of patience. {{note:{index:1048,id:UT22084-055-001-2955}}} Not seeing a thing that is tolerated, they are perfectly at peace. {{note:{index:1049,id:UT22084-055-001-2956}}} They are wise heroes who do not become proud of the strength of their patience. {{note:{index:1050,id:UT22084-055-001-2957}}} {9}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2958}} “They who know the peace that is the nature of phenomena, Never have in mind the idea ‘I am cutting through things’; For them all things are nonexistent, always empty, And they have eliminated every single conceptual identification. {10}
{{milestone:UT22084-055-001-2959}} “Such are they who teach the supreme nature of phenomena. They will before long reach the highest enlightenment. They comprehend the scope of the nature of phenomena. They give a gift that is infinite and endless. {11}
